52.    The working group of the Central Bank on interest rates and spreads focused particular
attention, in 2001, to the issue of the taxation of financial institutions and transactions and their
impact on spreads. Two working papers were issued on the role of the CPMP in the Brazilian
financial system, and made publicly available on the Central Bank's website.25 The reports
suggest that the CPMF results in fewer checks being issued, less financial transactions,
especially stock market transactions (thus decreasing its own base), higher interest rate spreads
and higher interest rates on government bonds (thus partly offsetting the revenue gain from the
CPMF).26 Given that the CPMF is not charged on transactions by mutual funds or on consumer
credit companies the tax encourages a shift away from sources of financing subject to CPMF
towards those which are exempted. While accepting that the CPM is necessary for fiscal
reasons, at the present juncture, its medium term efficiency issues need to be addressed. In April
2002, the proposal for the extension of the CPMF, in the form of a Constitutional
Amendment, was voted upon and passed by the Lower House of Congress, and embedded
25 The studies are: Impactos Economicos da CPMF: Teoria e Evidencia, by Pedro H. Albuquerque (June 2001), and
Os Efeitos da CPMF Sobre a IntermediaVdo Financeira, by Sergio Mikio Koyama and Marcio I. Nakane (July
2001).
26 Checks can be endorsed only once, but are nevertheless passed on - a common practice in Brazil. The Central
Bank expects this practice to go down after introduction of the RTGS payment system.
Page 18



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
in this bill is the exemption of CPMF for stock trades. This represents a major advance for
the rationalization of financial system taxation. Senate votes on the Bill are expected shortly.
53.   Given its lower fiscal importance (less than 2 percent of total revenue), less attention has
been devoted to the IOF, although the variance in its rate depending on loan maturity and the
discretionary character of the tax, are potentially distortive. The possibility of charging different
rates on different credit operations (as was the case until 1999) raises the risk of credit market
segmentation. IOF rates are regulated by the Central Bank.
54.   Also in April 2002, the government announced its intention to phase out the PIs and
COFINS; in a two stage reform which would transform the 0.65 percent PIS tax into a value-
added tax within 90 days and the 3 percent COFINS tax within 14 months. Given the fact
that until now these were levied on total revenues, i.e., a la cascade, the proposed new structure
would be more efficient for financial sector and other transactions.
55.   So far, the analysis of taxation and the financial sector undertaken by authorities in Brazil
has given relatively low attention to the impact of implicit taxation. Two critical vehicles through
which implicit taxation impacts upon the financial system are through (i) the high level of
unremunerated reserves and second through high requirements for directed credit. With regard to
the former, reserves were high in absolute terms even at the start of 2001, despite the major rate
reduction in 2000. Although also used as an instrument for monetary policy tightening, as in
September 2001, remuneration of reserves could help to level the playing field between different
types of financial instruments. Second, current policies of directed credit, which approximates
around 40 percent of total bank lending, also constitutes an implicit tax on the banking sector,
also adversely affecting overhead costs.
Financial Sector - Broad-Based Legislative Changes
56.   A recent Constitutional Amendment has great significance for financial sector
legislation in a number of areas. Constitutional Amendment 32 of September 11, 2001,
changed the rules for Medidas Provis6rias or provisional measures. Medidas Provis6rias are
instruments which can be issued by Presidential order and which have the force of law, until
rejected or adopted as laws by Congress. While sometimes useful for the speedy introduction of
legislation, in view of Congressional backlogs, they have the disadvantage of unclear legislative
sanction, due to the need, until the recent amendment for reenactment at frequent intervals to
maintain their validity. They are thus sometimes limited in acceptance, due to underlying
concerns about reversibility or non-renewal. Constitutional Amendment No. 32 provides that
new Medidas Provis6rias can only be extended once (for a total of 120 days). They have to be
voted by Congress during this period of 120 days, or the parliamentary agenda is held up. It also
clarifies that existing provisional measures may only be revoked by new provisional measures or
voted upon by Congress, which is no different from the rules regarding the revocation of laws in
general. Accordingly, former provisional measures, which already were considered as law
according to the Constitution, but which needed to be continuously re-enacted by the President,
will now be in force as law indefinitely. Given that a large number of law regulating economic
life and the financial system are in the form of a 'Medida Provisoria', the effective conversion of
existing Medida Provisorias into laws is an important legislative development.
Page 19



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
57.    One significant effect on the rmancial system of the Constitutional Amendment
pertaining to decree laws is the effective voiding of the Usury Law for institutions deemed
to be within the National Financial System. This historic law (Decree 22626 of President
Vargas in 1933) imposed a 12 percent annual cap on interest, and also, prohibited the charging
of interest on interest (i.e., the "capitalization" of interest charges) accrued during a period of less
than one year. This prohibition had been confirmed in several legal precedents, including its
application to financial institutions, until the passage of the law on financial institutions
(4595/64).27 Although the latter exempted financial institutions from the interest rate cap,
ambiguity was introduced again with the 1988 constitution which asked for a 12 percent cap on
real interest rates. Meanwhile, the capitalization of interest remained. This was finally lifted for
the operations of financial institutions, including in periods of less than one year, in March 31,
2000, according to Article 5 of Medida Provis6ria No. 2170-36 (re-enactment of provisional
measure No. 1963-19). With the passage of Amendment 32, this provisional measure is now in
force indefinitely and enjoys full legal status, with the historic result of rendering the usury law
irrelevant for formal financial institutions. Note however that the amendment of Article 192
would still be needed for the complete elimination of the 12 percent real interest cap, which is
currently still applicable to non-financial institutions, including for example the non-profit
entities operating in microfinance, or factoring companies which are outside the purview of
Central Bank supervision.
58.    Constitutional Amendment 32 has also had important consequences for an
important legal contract, the bank credit bond (Cedula do Cridito Bancdrio) also treated in a
provisional measure issued prior to the enactment. The bank credit bond was originally
established by Medida Provis6ria No. 1925, of October 14, 1999, which was continuously re-
enacted until the passage of Constitutional Amendment 32 of 2001. At the time of passage of the
Amendment, the bank credit bond was regulated by Medida Provis6ria No. 2160-25, of August
23, 2001, which became law from end-December 2001. Although the bank credit bond is
a convenient and safe credit transaction for financial institutions, it has been rarely used due to
the uncertainties of the conversion into law of the provisional measure which regulated these
bonds. Currently, there is no reason for any uncertainty due to the fact that the relevant
provisional measure has the force of law indefinitely, according to Amendment 32, and it is
hoped that the application of this instrument will now rise.28
59.    As flagged in the First Loan, a number of major reforms of the financial system have
been has been hitherto blocked by the absence of enabling legislation, due to constraints imposed
by Article 192 of the 1988 Constitution. This article had left a large number of complex but basic
financial sector issues (i.e. Central Bank independence, foreign bank entry, deposit insurance,
interest rate ceilings and regulatory and supervisory arrangements) to be regulated by a single
27 In Smsmula (Supreme Court decision) 121 of 1963, the Supreme Court decided that the limit on capitalization of
interest would apply to even financial institutions. The law on financial institutions (4595 of 1964) however
achieved the exemption of the 12 percent interest rate cap for financial institutions, on the ground that the Central
Bank could put ceilings on financial institutions. This was confirmed by Suimula 596 (of December 15, 1976). But
the restriction against capitalization remained until the passage of Medida Provis6ria 1925 of 2000.
28 The importance of the Cedula with regard to bank credit is discussed further below, in the context of the
importance of contract enforcement.
Page 20



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
enabling law (Lei Complementar) at a later date.29 Despite several attempts since 1988 at
regulating Article 192, ultimately a lack of legislative consensus blocked progress. The passage
of a Constitutional Amendment to permit regulation of Article 192 through a set of laws
accelerated towards the end of 2001. Senate approval as well as approval by specialized
subcommittees of the House have been secured.
60.    The amendment would also enable the presentation to Congress of a 'minimalist' but
powerful new Central Bank Law, which institutionalizes the Central Bank's monetary policy
autonomy and accountability; and could be as far-reaching as the Lei de Responsibilidade Fiscal
is for fiscal policy autonomy. This brief law will specify the objective(s) the Central Bank should
pursue and establish operational autonomy of the Central Bank in pursuing the objective(s).
Credit Contracts and Expanded Access to Housing Finance
61.    As noted in the documentation for the first Financial Sector Adjustment Loan to Brazil,
the inefficiency of the legal system and poor enforcement of credit contracts has contributed to
high overhead costs of financial transactions. One of the government's contributions towards
improving contract enforcement was through the introduction of the Aliena,do Fiduci6ria
instrument (fiduciary alienation), through the creation of a trust, similar to chattel mortgage);
originally introduced in 1969 (Decree Law 911, Article 66) for consumer, especially car
financing. Unlike other secured credit (and as in conditional sale and in leasing contracts) the
ownership and title is transferred to a trust, and the creditor has the first claim on the assets of the
trust.30 In the case of default, the creditor can get a search-and-seize order to consolidate title
and possession. It has worked relatively well for car financing and has also been used in business
financing.
62.   Fiduciary alienation was also introduced for real estate financing in the context of efforts
to improve the Real Estate Financial System in 1997 (Law 9514 on the Sistema Financeiro
Imobilidrio, SFI). Although not widely used in this context, due to other difficulties in the
launching of real estate reforms, the Supreme Court upheld it as constitutional in 1998. Wider
use of the Aliena,do began in the first half of 2001, when the Caixa Econ6mica Federal first
began to use it systematically, as part of its improved credit risk management policy, in tandem
with credit scoring This inspired other housing lenders to also issue contracts based on this
instrument. Most banks have not yet tested this new collateral but their preliminary feedback
seems to be positive. It should also be noted that out-of-the-court mortgage foreclosure
proceedings have been upheld as constitutional and would also permit faster debt.
63.    A recent Medida Provisdria (No. 2223 of September 4, 2001) extends the use of the
Alienafdo in the context of housing finance, by permitting new housing related securities,
which can be backed by real estate credits collateralized by the traditional mortgage or the newly
created fiduciary alienation (Aliena,do Fiducidria). The new credit instrument, the "Letra de
29 An ordinary law needs a simple majority vote of persons present for passage; a Lei Complementar requires a
simple majority of all members (lower or upper house), not only members present and finally, a constitutional
amendment requires a two thirds majority of two sessions of all members.
30 Title is transferred to a trust, technically, but the creditor has the first claim on the assets of the trust.
Page 21



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
Cr6dito Imobilirio - LCI" may be issued by commercial banks and universal banks in addition
to the Caixa, and also by savings and loans institutions and real estate credit societies. The
additional guarantee made of collateralized real estate credits should enhance the bond rating,
and therefore reduce the costs of funds of the lending institution. The LCI significantly is
allowed to contain monthly indexation clauses (not limited to the TR index that is now lower
than inflation) in order to be more attractive for investors. These can be used to finance any form
of housing loan (i.e., they are not limited to new construction). The usual seignorage in
bankruptcy claims of these mortgage bonds however remains an unresolved legal challenge. 31
64.   As mentioned in the first PFSECAL documentation, the government had created a new
lending contract; the Cedula de Credito Bancdrio, which is a security that represents a bank
credit - i.e., an asset-backed security where the underlying asset represented bank claims.32 It
fulfills requirements to permit execution of title (titulo executivo), i.e., the underlying debt does
not have to be recognized by a court. It also allows for securitization of the claim. The Cedula
was first introduced by a Medida Provis6ria 1925 on October 14, 1999, and has been regularly
extended since then. However it was not been used widely, due to banks' concerns regarding the
non-renewal of the Medida Provis6ria. With the recent passage of Constitutional
Amendment No. 32, this measure now enjoys full legal status, and wider use has already
begun, as evidenced by recent court judgments.
65.   In addition, the use of the C6dula has also been expanded, for the first time in 2001,
to the real estate finance sector, through a new instrument, the Cedula de Credito
Imobilidrio - CCI, which may be issued by institutions other than banks, such as real estate
companies in order to sell its real estate credit receivables. Similar to the Cedula de Cr&dito
Bancdrio, the new instrument is a security structured as a legal vehicle to represent a real estate
credit. CCI can be quoted and traded on the secondary market, using the same clearing
arrangements as for private equities; the CETIP system, helping to reduce transactions costs.
Also, construction companies can include monthly indexation clauses for real estate financing
contracts previously allowed only for financial institutions' credits. This allows construction
companies to better match their assets and liabilities. The CCI can also be acquired by
securitization companies that may later issue mortgage-backed-securities with the appropriate
standardization, documentation and credit enhancements. The extension of this instrument to real
estate companies who represent a significant share of housing credits in Brazil is of significance
in the context of the development of the housing finance market, as it encourages the expansion
of the market for housing loans beyond the banking system, where this market segment has been
dominated by Caixa Econ6mica Federal, encouraging the development of a market-based market
segment distinct from the subsidized segment which dominates the operations of the Caixa
31 LCIs may be bought by securitization companies, who can then issue for the first time, genuine mortgage backed
securities based on these, with appropriate enhancements, etc.
32 World Bank Report No. P7448-BR; April 26, 2001, on the First Programmatic Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
Page 22



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
Economica Federal. It is hoped that these recent developments will widen the housing finance
market and foster the development of securitized real estate lending.33
66.    At the same time, the concept of the Patrim6nio de afetacdo, a trust-like institution, was
also introduced (Medida Provis6ria 2221 of September 4, 2001) for real estate financing. This
legal construction separates assets of a construction company for a specific real estate project,
from the assets of the company itself, so that they are not a part of claims against the company in
the event of its bankruptcy, and it serves to give greater security to participants in housing
schemes, as well as housing finance plans sponsored by constructors.34 Together, these measures
considerably clarify, strengthen as well as deepen and extend the use of more enforceable credit
contracts in different segments of the financial system.
67.    The creation of instruments/ vehicles for securitization (of housing finance assets as well
as other asset-backed securities in general) was further enriched at the end of 2001 by the
introduction of Credit Investment Funds (FIDC - fiundos de investimento em direitos credit6rios
introduced in the CVM's Instruction 356 of December 17, 2001); funds which can hold securities
based on any credit receivables including real estate mortgages. The fund's shares correspond to
a proportion of the credit pool receivables. The shares must be rated every quarter and their
accounting value re-assessed every month. They can be listed and traded on the stock exchange
or over-the-counter. They are reserved for professional investors. The fund may be closed or
open. Differentiated payment rights can be attached to the shares, in order to permit credit
enhancement. This special MBS/ABS vehicle represents a considerable simplification of the
current securitization process, which would require the costly creation of a publicly listed
securitization company.35 Moreover, the FDIC is exempted from various financial system taxes
- the CPMF as well as PIS / COFINS), as are other investment funds.36 Together, these measures
considerably clarify, strengthen as well as deepen and extend the use of more enforceable credit
contracts in different segments of the financial system.

feeds into overhead costs and thus bank spreads. A major upgrading of the Central de Risco
is under implementation. The Risk Center has already begun to gather information on loans
of a smaller denomination than hitherto - R$5,000 is now the threshold of data availability,

under implementation. The upgrading of the Risk Center, with its expanded coverage and
reduced loan size threshold is important for access to information on small clients, and
thus has huge potential for facilitating access to credit for small borrowers.
69.    An important step in the strengthening of creditor rights will be the passage of an
amended Bankruptcy law (Lei de Falencias). A draft law ("Biolchi project") has been ready to
be voted upon in the House for several years (since 1993); however it was widely acknowledged
that the proposals had many serious limitations. Amendments to further strengthen the draft
were proposed by the Central Bank over the course of 2001, and a revamped and
considerably strengthened version is now being brought before the House.40 The bill is being
supported with renewed impetus and likelihood of its passage has also increased.
37 The threshold was reduced from R$50,000 to R$20,000 in October 1999 and to R$5,000 in early 2001.
38 The inclusion of SCMs among institutions with reporting requirements to the Risk Center was announced in
Resolution 2874 of the National Monetary Council (26 July 2001). Annex 3 has more details.
39 Financed under the Bank's technical assistance loan to the Central Bank, the quality-and-cost based selection for
consultant services for the final extension of the Risk Center System was completed in September and a contract
has now been awarded. The extended system is expected to be operational in the fall of 2002.
40 The Bank has been critically involved in these revisions though an advisory process launched with a ROSC on
bankruptcy in the fall of 2001.

Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
The Draft Bankruptcy Law
In the current law there are no provisions for rwancial and/or operational restructuring but only for debt
suspension for a period of time (cbncordata suspensiva). Reforms proposed in the TBiolchi' project -introduce
restructuring with possibility of sale of individual assets, shifting the focus from the protection of the debtor to.
the preservation of the business, if *iable, through the  `recuperaqdo judic'a abolishing completely the
concordata which had unnecessarily prolonged liquidations. This process would allow for a much broader range
of options to maintain the businress, such as the possibility of partial sale of assets, rnerger and acquisition,
substitution of management, increase in capital stock, collective labor agreements etc. However, abolishing the
concordaia has the disadvantage of taking away a flexible instrument for enterprises that face' temporary'liquidity
problems. Revised proposals offer an e-xtended menufor enterprises in difficulties.
Currently, creditors do not participate in the process of liquidation or concordata. While Lhe judicial liquidator
has to consult creditors according to the current law, (s)he usually does not do so, and there is no instituuonal
arrangement, such as a creditor committee. The Biolchi project therefore proposes to institute a Comite de
Recuperac,o, comprising the judicial administrator, one employee, and one representative each from the class oft
secured and unsecured creditors. This comnuttee has the authority to present an alternative restructunng plan,'
',supervise the debtor dunng restructuring and evaluate creditor claims. However, even tlFis proposal niay leave
ercessive power to the 'judge who can in,principle accept a restructuring plan proposed by the debtor aind
rejected by ilie creditors.
There are further limitations in the proposed draft law due to, tax debts and labor charges. According to the
C6digo Tributdrio Ntacional (Article 187), tax debts are not subject to bankruptcy and restructuring.
processes, i.e. the enterprise or its successor are liable for.tax debts up to five vears after the respective lax year,"
even if these were not claimed by the'revenue service at the nme of succession; Changes intax provisions have lbo
be introduced in the C6digo Tributdrio Nacional, which -is a complementarv law and therefore requires a
qualified majority in Congress for any changes.'lt is p'roposed in the'new revisions to limit tax liabilities to the'
ones that are registered at the time of bankruptcy or succession, or to limit tax debt to the principal and exempL
any interest charges and other penalties on tax debt. Claims by employees against the company are currently
u,nlimited, extend to' the successor of the company, and rank first in the creditor priority. The Biolchi project
.proposes, on the one hand, to elevate the Fundo de Garantia por Tempo de Serviqo (severance find) to the status
'of a priority creditor, but, on the other hand, to lImit all claims from labor' indemnification and severance pay to
R$30,000 per employee. Other proposals aim to' limit' labor,charges zo three or sir months of salary of ihe
respective employee.               ,              ,    - '                      ' '   ,         '
Under the current law in force, new credits granted under concordata have Lhe same status 'as other credits if the.'
company goes into bankruptcy, which is a strong disincentive for any creditor td grant additional resources to a
firm that is under concordata: The'proposed Biolchi project would give these creditors priority if a company
under restructuring goes into liquidation.  '
70.     Positive aspects of the 'Biolchi' project included (i) increased flexibility to restructuring
and liquidation, going well beyond the present sole measure for debt suspension (concordata
suspensiva). Indeed the Biolchi project aimed at the elimination of the concordata. The Biolchi
project also (ii) increased priority to new creditors during restructuring and (iii) allowed
accelerated asset sales of a firm in the process of liquidation by allowing sales of the company as
a whole.
Page 25



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
71.   However, shortcomings of the 'Biolchi project' were (i) the continued limits on
participation of creditors in the restructuring and liquidation process; (ii) its failure to prioritize
labor and tax claims, (iii) lack of time limits on the standstill period, and (iv) lack of sufficient
attention to problems in asset sales.
72.   Recent amendments made to the draft address these areas of difficulties by (i) enhancing
creditor participation by the creation of a Creditor's Assembly which would accompany the
restructuring or liquidation activity, and requiring formal approval of the creditor's plan by such
an assembly by a majority of at least three creditor classes, (ii) imposing limits on labor claims
to R$30,000 and (iii) establishing the principle that even in the absence of changes in the Tax
code which would be necessary to address the issue of tax claims, such claims should be limited
in amount and protection against such claims should be given to would-be purchasers; (iii)
limiting the standstill period (time between demand by debt for restructuring and approval of
restructuring plan by creditor assembly) to 90 days (or 45 days plus one extension of another 45
days). It also plans to sanction the concept of extrajudicial liquidation, for larger enterprises, and
create special panels for small enterprises' debt rescheduling; and (iv) give a larger menu of for
sale, and also, more options for small enterprises.
73.   In sum, looking at progress with regard to the achievement of an overall increase in the
efficiency and depth of intermediation, it must be acknowledged that much has been done, but
much also remains to be done. In particular, the major legal reforms of Article 192 and
amendments to the financial systems law remain poised on the brink of achievement, but as
political uncertainty mounts towards the end of the term of the present administration, they may
be difficult to achieve. And while many measures have been adopted to raise the depth and
efficiency of financial intermediation, remaining high spreads and real interest rates, albeit in
part the result of exogenous factors, are still to be brought into a more realistic range.
THE BANKING SYSTEM AND ITS RECENT EVOLUTION
Performnance Update
74.   Details of the underlying structure of Brazil's banking system as well as changes it has
undergone since the Real plan have been discussed in the loan documentation for the first
financial sector adjustment loan, which noted the trend reduction in the overall numbers of
banks, the sharp increase in foreign bank presence, and the parallel reduction in the presence of
state-owned banks, over the period 1995-2000. The present section therefore first provides a
brief update on structural and performance trends in Brazil's banking system over the past year,
and then focuses on recent significant initiatives for structural change in publicly owned banks.
75.   In terms of trend structural change, the wave of bank mergers and consolidations which
began in 1997 gained further momentum in 2001 and is expected to accelerate further in 2002.
Initiated by losses in 'float' income, which followed the decline of inflation from the mid-1990s,
and the introduction in 1994 of minimum capital requirements, the trend decline in interest rates
and spreads in the last two to three years has also exerted a downward pressure on bank interest
income, (from their government securities portfolios) and income from spreads, and has led to
compensating increases in volumes of loans and securities held. This, together with reductions in
public sector borrowing, has increased the relative importance of loan volume, as a source of
Page 26



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
income and profits. The consequence has been not only rapid loan growth but also a increase in
the importance of operational scale, and hence, of interest in the acquisition of public and private
banks, leading also to a trend acceleration in the premia of privatizations, which is discussed in
further detail below. As the last wave of privatization of state-owned banks is now concluding,
mergers and buyouts of state bank branches and private banks, both domestic and foreign, is
likely to continue in 2002, as private banks scramble to consolidate their shares.
76.   Looking at recent performance, Brazil's banking system as a whole remains generally
sound, despite some signs of strain in mid-2001. Despite a contraction of net banking sector
income in June 2001, reflecting the restructuring of the federally owned Caixa, net income for
the banking sector as a whole recovered rapidly towards the end of the year. Net income of
R$7.8 billion in December 2001 are more than double the corresponding figure for December
2000 (R$3.3 billion).4' Over half the total profits (53.9 percent or R$4.2 billion) were achieved
by the five major private banks, Bradesco, Itaui, Santander, Unibanco and ABN Amro Bank, in
that order. Analysts observe that the main factors behind the sustained profitability of the
banking system were partly the result of foreign exchange gains, treasury gains from securities
operations due to rising interest rates, and expanded lending. It is noteworthy that income from
securities operations grew 32.1 percent during the year to R$32.1 billion (US$13.76 billion),
while gains from credit operations grew only 10.3 percent to R$47.1 billion (US$20.2 billion) in
2001. Aggregate banking sector data up to end December shows a decline in the proportion of
interest income from loans and leases, from 60 percent to 55.1 percent of total interest income,
over the year, with a corresponding increase in interest income from securities (34.1 percent to
37.4 percent) and some increase of the share of foreign exchange income (from 4.1 percent to 5
percent).42
77.   Looking at federal versus private banks, in terms of sources of income, data for the
federal banks shows dramatic changes, with a huge decline in the proportion of interest income
from loans and leases, from a high of 75.6 percent to 51 percent of total interest income, with a
doubling in interest income from securities (18.8 percent to 37.7 percent) and some increase in
interest income from the share of foreign exchange (from 0.3 percent to 4.4 percent). These data
reflect the restructuring and write off of large volumes of bad assets, and their replacement by
government securities.43 The data for the private banks shows no significant change in the
proportion of interest income from loans and leases, down slightly from 60.8 percent (December
2000) to 60.4 percent of total interest income (December 2001), a small decrease in interest
income from securities (36.4 percent to 32.4 percent) and an increase in the share of foreign
exchange (from 4.4 percent to 5.9 percent). A reduced rate of currency depreciation in early 2002
could reduce profitability as well as impact upon efficiency and asset quality indicators. Brazil's
banks today are more sensitive towards asset quality changes than a few years ago, due to high
loan growth in recent years, and loan quality may be affected by the economic slowdown.
41 All data and estimates are undertaken by the World Bank staff, based on data from the Central Bank, unless
otherwise stated.
42 It is held that foreign exchange gains may be understated. Unfortunately a breakdown or explanation is not
available. It is likely that these have accrued through hedging against the expected devaluation of the real.
43 Accrued income from non-performing loans would no longer be recorded.

Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
largest five federal banks shrunk somewhat between December 1999 and December 2000, from
R$135 billion to R$131 billion, and then declined further dramatically by December 2001, to
R$103 billion or by 23.7 percent. Private bank lending, which had escalated more rapidly in the
recent period (R$61 billion to R$82 billion from December 1999 to December 2000, almost 35
percent), continued to grow, at a somewhat diminished rate, to a further R$107 billion in
December 2001 (almost 31 percent).
79.   The share of loans in total assets for the banking system as a whole declined in 2001,
from to 32.2 percent in December 1999 to 31.8 percent in December 2000, to 29.6 percent in
December 2001. However this can be attributed to declines in federal banks, and reflects
substantially their financial restructuring and impaired asset write offs. For the top five federal
banks, loans to total assets declined from 39.1 percent in December 1999 to 34.9 percent in
December 2000, and as may be expected with the mid-year clean up and recapitalization, to 26.1
percent in December 01), with a parallel increase in assets held as securities (19.3 percent to 29.6
percent). Loan to asset ratios have increased for large private banks. By contrast, for the banking
system as a whole, deposit growth, which had been slow in 2000 (with virtually no change
between the R$316 billion of December 1999 and R$318 billion of December 2000) grew 16.2
percent to R$ 369.6 billion in December 2001. The corresponding decline in loan deposit ratios
and loan asset ratios implies some increase in liquidity; loan-deposit ratios declined over the last
year from 93.9 percent in December 2000 to 85.2 percent in December 2001.
80.   Finally, indicators of changes in asset quality have been relatively stable. Using the
Central Bank's newly generated loan classification data, it is shown that in December 2001,
loans classified as 'normal' (AAA to C) amounted to 88.2 percent of total loans outstanding, and
showed little variation over the previous year." Loans in the Risk 1 category (D to G) did show
some trend increase over the year (8 percent in December 2001, up from 7.2 percent in June
2001, and from 6.3 percent in December 2000. However loans in the worst (Risk 2 or H)
category correspondingly declined (3.7 percent in December 2001, down from 4.1 percent in
June 2001 and from 5.9 percent in December 2000). According to private analysts of the top 17
banks (representing around 75 percent of the banking system), the share of non-performing loans
in gross loans declined over the year, from 7.6 percent in December 1999 to 4.9 percent in
December 2000, and further to 2.9 percent by June 2001. Capital adequacy ratios accordingly
have remained broadly robust, varying from 9.4 percent in December 1999 with some decline to
8.9 percent in December 2000 and recovering to 9.2 percent in December 2001.
PuBLIc BANK REFORM AND RESTRUCTURING
81.   The recent acceleration of Brazil's program of public bank reform is a major step
forward in a process which had its genesis in a program of bank strengthening which began in
1995, shortly after the launching of the Real plan.45 The PROER and PROES programs for the
restructuring of private and state govemment owned financial institutions, aimed at preventing
44 This figure is down slightly from the June 2001 figure of 88.7 percent, but up slightly on the year to year
December 2000 figure of 87.9 percent.
45 See Annex 2 for details on both federal and state bank reforms, including programs initiated at individual federal
banks.
Page 29



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
financial crises, enhancing financial system soundness and integrity as well as protecting against
fiscal indiscipline at the state level.46 The new step forward in reform, launched in June
2001, for the first time address problems at the country's largest, federally-owned financial
institutions. These initiatives are backed by new prudential regulations and greatly
strengthened banking supervision which requires compliance with regulatory norms at the
federal-banks, and also requires the government as owner to take cognizance and action to
ensure the solvency of federal financial institutions. Recent actions however may be viewed
as the first phase of a further series of measures to ensure sustainability of recent actions.
Federal Banks
82.   Brazil's four deposit taking federally owned financial institutions include the Banco do
Brasil (BdB) and the Caixa Economica Federal (CEF), which are the two largest deposit banks in
the country, and two smaller regional federal banks, the Banco do Nordeste do Brasil (BNB), and
Banco da Amaz8nia - BASA.  Over the years, these banks, which have been used to implement
specially designed and targeted programs for lending to specific sections of the economy
(notably rural and housing finance programs and regional development programs), have suffered
continued deterioration of their loan portfolio, as a result of a combination of factors; their
special mandates and programs, limited supervision and inspection, differential norms for the
roles of managers and keeping of accounts for federal banks relative to private banks, and also,
the problems of internal efficiency and unclear accountability.
83.   Following the issue of a series of new prudential regulations for the banking system from
1999, and the major improvements introduced in its systems of on-site bank examination and
supervision, the Central Bank of Brazil launched a comprehensive program of on-site
examinations which revealed problems that have existed in the four banks for years; a significant
proportion of which were due to credit operations that the federal banks make on behalf of the
federal government. Negotiations between the government, as owner of the Federal Banks, and
the Central Bank, as regulator and supervisor, resulted in a series of decisions, enshrined in a
Decree Law of June 22, 2001, to restructure and recapitalize the federal banks, and going
forward, to introduce transparency in their operations with the government.48
84.   The main objectives spelled out in this law were to require the owner (the State) to
restore the financial condition of these banks, recognizing and absorbing past losses. Going
forward the Federal Government undertakes to assume the risks and costs of the various federal
credit programs managed by these institutions, reflecting transparently in its budget any
subsidies provided through these banks, which henceforth must be approved by the National
Congress. The Decree Law provides specifically for:
46The PROES program for restructuring state banks was launched in August 1996.
47 The fifth federal bank, and the third largest in terms of size, is the BNDES, the National Development Bank.
However, it does not take deposits from the public.
48 Medida Provisoria No. 2196-1, issued on June 22, 2001.
Page 30



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
* Removing the credit risk from the operations funded by the so called "Constitutional
Funds" managed by these banks prior to November 30, 1998;49
* Allowing these banks to manage new "Constitutional Funds" at their own risk. The
banks can decide whether or not they wish to share the credit risk of such loans, receiving
higher returns if they agree to bear such risks;50
* Authorizing the Government to void guarantees given by the federal banks for rural
credits sold to the Federal Government at book value. Thus these banks would not bear
any further responsibility for credit risk on the rural and real estate loans swapped with the
Federation for new, negotiable, debt;5'
* Authorizing the Federation to net out the debit and credit accounts of the federal
banks with the Federation;
* Establishing special debt-for-bond swap programs for various programs/debts held by
each of the four federal banks.
85.    The recapitalization actions undertaken to execute the "Medida Provis6ria" are intended
to constitute the first stage of a transformation process which aims to have the federal banks
governed more independently, with their senior managers accountable to commercially oriented
performance targets, which are better specified and communicated internally, and determined in
advance within the framework of each institutions' strategic plan. The overall transformation
process therefore also envisages internal changes which will constitute a second phase of
reorganization, to be incorporated in their strategic planning process for the 2002-04 triennial.
Specifically, the internal changes, actively supported and closely monitored by the Central Bank,
are envisaged to include:
* Leveraging management layers by creating a structure of accountability with
decentralized reporting, providing for more objective and commercial decision making;
* Developing a new commercial strategy and new products to diversify away from their
traditional targeted sectors and Government-oriented programs;
* Organizing activities by major business lines and separating out Government-related
activities;
* Improving management information systems to support the monitoring of the above
actions and to view the performance of each major business line, especially for
49 There are three regional Constitutional funds, managed by three of the four FFI; the North-East fund, (managed
by BNB), the Northern fund (managed by BASA), and the Center-East fund (managed by BdB). These funds have
been used as vehicles for the implementation of social policy objectives through credit allocation, channeling funds
to certain activities designated by the government.
50 Under option (i) the bank would assume 100 percent of the credit risk and receive a 6 percent return from the
Constitutional Fund. It would also be permitted to consider funds received as part of its Tier 2 capital (subordinated
debt) subject to the overall limit that Tier 2 capital cannot exceed 50 percent of the banks' Tier 1 capital. Under
option (ii) the bank only assumes 50 percent of the credit risk, receives a lower return (3 percent), and cannot deem
funds received to be part of its Tier 2 capital. The main beneficiary of the first option is likely to be Banco do Brasil.
51 Includes transactions related to FUNCAFE,, PRODECER II and other credits.
Page 31



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
Government programs, hence enabling performance monitoring on a risk adjusted
basis;
* Improving internal controls according to plans, and within a timetable required by the
Central Bank.
86.   Clearly, these actions may be viewed as significant and major first steps towards the
reform of the largest financial institutions in Brazil. Based on the underlying new prudential
requirements, continued enforcement of compliance of these regulations will help to ensure that
financial soundness is sustained, and that the inflow of new public funds is not wasted. The
decision to inject new government securities in the institutions which are liquid and remunerated
at market rates is also a significant advance over early attempts at financial bailouts over a
decade ago, provided the banks are indeed permitted free use of these resources. Decisions to
increase the transparency of government mandates are laudable. The adoption of the phased
program to simultaneously reform internal controls, audit, management information and
governance systems will be the key to reform sustainability.
87.   Nevertheless, many problem areas remain. Financial restructuring which has already
taken place could not solve all the financial problems facing the banks; in particular the
accounting of tax credits, as well as the adequacy of pension provisions are likely remaining
problems - although these known to be possible problem areas in private banks as well. There
are also specific details in some accounts which will take considerable work of precision to fully
account for, which could have implications for projected future income streams.52 There is also
considerable variation between the four federal banks, and clearly difficulties at some are
considerably larger than at others. Custom designed solutions will be needed to address these.
88.   Going forward, several challenges lie ahead to ensure the sustainability of reforms.
This will require close cooperation and a shared vision between the government as the owner,
the Central Bank as the banking supervisor, and senior management at the banks. First, the
government as owner needs to ensure that directors serving on the boards of the federal banks
are suitably qualified professionals, with the independence to support and oversee the execution
of the internal changes that are being initiated. Today, standard fit-and-proper criteria for private
bank directors are not applicable to public banks. Regulatory requirements on governance,
fitness and enforcement should ideally be achieved by incorporation into the by-laws of public
banks. Political risks in this agenda cannot be underestimated; the government as both owner and
controlling shareholder plays a pivotal role.
89.   Second, senior management of the federal financial institutions needs to adopt a viable
and commercial business strategy that optimizes the potential of their banking franchise,
including the real capital to finance it, and systems which allow the Boards to control, and the
Central Bank to monitor, its execution. This would include the real separation of lines of
business, with appropriate allocations of overheads and full cost accounting for each, a clear
accounting separation of government activities. It should include measures to address the poor
52 e.g., at Caixa, future income will be affected also by the prospects of its CVS paper which will become due in the
future, the real value and projected future value of income from judicial deposits, its ability to cope with credit risk
in the future as lending will need to expand, etc.
Page 32



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
efficiency of both banks and rationalize their costs structures without relying solely on gains
from business volumes.
90.   Third, the Central Bank has to augment the scope of its supervisory approach to
enforce best standards and also to add qualitative judgment in evaluating and monitoring the
new strategy and accompanying financial and capital plans of the federal financial institutions.
The Central Bank would need to achieve this without diminishing the surveillance and
examination efforts to assess their continuous solvency.
91.   The Central Bank is aware of these challenges and has begun to prepare a phased
action program of medium term restructuring and rehabilitation for the four deposit
taking federal banks. The Central Bank is enthusiastic about the addition of monitoring
indicators to such a program, which would be agreed with the government, as principal
shareholder of the federal financial institutions. Such phased action programs could differ for
each specific institution, as there are wide differentials in their present status, with regard to
performances as well as internal controls.
92.   To achieve a better understanding of specific problem areas, a second round of
follow up inspections of all four federal banks was initiated in early 2002, and is expected to
be completed by May this year. These follow up inspections are focused on specific problem
areas: quality of management information systems, internal audit functions and processes, credit
risk models used internally, other risk management functions and processes, and also, a partial
credit review. Reforms proposed also include the strengthening of governance throuAh a decree
on the govemance of all government owned companies with Boards of Directors, and also,
eventually, through the passage of a Lei Complementar which would amend the fundamental
banking and financial system law 4595 of 1964, removing specific passages singling out specific
federal banks such as BNDES and Banco do Brasil for special treatment, as well as other
provisions affecting bank govemance, penalties, etc.
93.   A key issue in the area of public bank reform will be the continuation of political
consensus to move ahead. The government, as owner of the federal financial institutions, has
considerable authority over the appointment of bank boards, and at present, the Central Bank
does not have sufficient independence to ensure that its agenda of reform will be maintained if it
current reform oriented technical staff should change. These concems must be acknowledged.
Efforts are being made through the institution of increased disclosure and transparency in
decisions to maintain a steady course by public knowledge and support. The recent
announcement of the government in April 2002 of its intention to increase the proportion of
widely held shares in Banco do Brasil (from its present level of 8.7 percent to 25 percent)
for its eventual listing on the Novo Mercado is an example of its policies to enhance
disclosure to build reform momentum. The government has also announced its intention of
calling an Extraordinary Shareholders Assembly meeting to amend the statutes of Banco do
Brasil to enable this.
53 This would apply to both the joint public-private companies (Sociedades de Economia Mista) such as Banco do
Brasil, BNB and BASA, as well as to the public companies (Empresas Puiblicas, such as Caixa Econ6mica Federal)
Page 33



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
State Banks
94.    Brazil's sustained and successful program of state bank restructuring and privatization
suggests that, provided political commitment remains unshaken, federal bank reform can also
make significant progress. At the launching of the state bank reform program, PROES, there
were 35 State-owned financial institutions, while as of end-March 2002, 10 State banks had been
liquidated, 14 banks had either been fully privatized (10 banks), or had been "federalized" as a
prior step to their privatization (4 banks). Out of the 14 banks 7 were being privatized directly by
the States and 7 by the Federal Government. Five state banks had been recapitalized and a large
number (16) of State Development Agencies, some of which were previously financial
institutions (either banks or former savings and loans) were put into operation.
95.    The pace of privatization of the state banks is accelerating. After the privatization of
BANESPA in November 2000, there was a long interval before the next privatization, of
Paraf'ba, in November 2001. Another three privatizations have since been concluded, in
November and December 2001 and January 2002. Four banks are still in federal hands and plans
for their privatization are advanced. It is expected that the privatization of state banks will be
concluded in the present year. Meanwhile, an additional Bank, still in state hands, has applied for
inclusion in the programs for privatization.54 It is expected that before the end of the term of
the present government, the privatization programs for state banks will be completed.
96.    The sale of the State banks has so far yielded R$11,482 billions (close to US$4.6 billion),
out of which 62.4 percent came from the sale of a single large bank, BANESPA.55 Most of the
funds are being used to net out State debts with the Federal Government, including funds to
recapitalize restructured state banks.
BANK SUPERvIsIoN AND BANK FAILURE RESOLuTioN
Supervision
97.    The Central Bank's progress with strengthened supervision, noted at the time of the
First Adjustment Loan, is sustained. Following improvements in loan classification, efforts are
being made to improve disclosure and internal controls.56 Steady even if slow progress in
program areas must be acknowledged, even if this is only a part of a long agenda. In terms of
specific projects discussed with the Central bank a year ago, significant progress can first of all
be noted with regard to the offsite supervision project, which is now ready. The new system

98.   Third, the project for the enhancement of the Credit Risk Center has also been
launched. The Center has already begun to extend the range of information it provides, from the
threshold of R$20,000, down to R$5,000. The current expansion under way would permit the
Central Bank to also develop and manage a model to assess systemic credit risk, as well as to be
able to gather and disseminate an enriched set of information for users (including positive
information).,The Risk Center has also expanded the scope of information it collects to
include a ran e of small institutions, including microfinance enterprises (SCMs) and credit
cooperatives.   The large scale and ambitious expansion project should be completed by
November 2002. The fourth significant project, developing and making operational a Bank
rating model began in October 2001, and it is expected that the contract will be completed by
July/August 2002. It is planned that rating standards will be formally approved by the Monetary
Council, and the Central Bank will publish the rating methodology, which is expected to closely
approximate the CAMvIELS rating system (i.e., it should incorporate not only financial ratios, but
the assessment by examiners on the quality and efficiency of the control and risk management
systems that support corporate governance) and to be integrated into the on-site and off-site
supervisory processes. The Central Bank supports the need to communicate relevant standards
for risk management and control systems to both boards of directors and senior management of
banks, to encourage enforcement. It intends that the new rating system should be advanced
enough to be applicable in terms of the future BIS 2 requirements.
99.   One area in which progress is slower than hoped for is with regard to the legal
protection of supervisors. While there is a very strong desire on the part of the Central Bank's
directors to pass such a law, which would encompass protection not only to bank supervisors but
also to officers and directors / Board members of the Central Bank, the present political juncture
is viewed as unfavorable for either its submission or its passage. Enhanced protection to senior
most supervisors in the draft Central Bank law to be submitted to Congress would however be
extended, through its provisions for autonomy and independence of Central Bank directors.
However protection to supervisors is still a long way away. In overall terms, while better
supervision practices in Brazil are steadily being developed, outstanding issues remain and also,

100. More progress has been made over the last year with Brazil's program of
accounting reform for financial institutions and with other areas of regulatory reform,
especially for securities and derivatives. Regulatory initiatives for calendar year 2002 focus on
two areas, dealing with accounting and risk management standards.
101.   The first type of changes intend to facilitate the convergence of current Regulatory
Accounting Practices mandated by the Central Bank (RAP) for financial institutions, towards
International Accounting Standards (IAS), a process that the Central Bank sees proceeding to
conclusion during the next two to five years. In addition, regulatory accounting practices that
relate to risk management intend to complement the changes that the Central Bank is introducing
in its approach to supervision and also to finalize the recent strengthening of federal financial
institutions. Recent achievements in this direction include a change in the regulation dealing with
the valuation and disclosure of securities, requiring securities to be marked to market, and
requiring also a distinction between securities held for cash, trading, or holding to maturity.59
Second, the Central Bank has several additional initiatives in the area of convergence between
Brazilian RAPs and IAS. The treatment of financial derivative securities and related
transactions is another area where some changes have been introduced and more are
contemplated. Netting of derivative obligations is allowed, derivatives are to be marked to
market, and hedge accounting has been strengthened by requiring the specification of credit
versus market risk hedges.60 As pointed out by Central Bank staff, Brazilian accounting may
differ from that required by IAS because of the absence of specific Brazilian rules on recognition
and measurement in specific areas, and on disclosure requirements. However, plans to rectify
these are underway.61
102.   A caveat to be added to the assessment of the overall situation of bank supervision is that
a more exhaustive view of the present situation in bank supervision is likely to emerge following
the joint Bank-IMF FSAP which has just been launched. It is hoped that this will more precisely
identify areas for further strengthening and of remaining risk.

Bank Failure Resolution
103.  Key current components of the bank failure resolution and deposit insurance framework
are described in the documentation for the First Programmatic Loan. To summarize, the
backbone of the system is Law 9447 which gives the Central Bank strong powers and significant
flexibility to deal with undercapitalized and insolvent banks; i.e., powers to require prompt
capital injections by shareholders or a solution via the merger with, or acquisition by, other
banks in the system. Failing that, the Central Bank enjoys powers to close the troubled bank and
immediately resolve it by splitting it into a "good" bank (containing good assets and the
liabilities with the public) to be sold/transferred to other banks, and a residual "bad" bank to
move onto extra-judicial liquidation. These tools have been used effectively recently for the
sale/merger of two medium-sized banks. The process of extra-judicial liquidation, which is
governed by Law 6024 of 1974, has however turned out to be an important drawback of the
current framework. The initial objective of this law-to increase the efficiency of liquidation
by taking it out of the judicial system and entrusting it to the Central Bank-has not been met.
The original idea of extra-judicial liquidation by the Central Bank (Law 6024, 1974) was that it
would be faster than judicial liquidation, that the Central Bank had better knowledge of banks,
that the Central Bank used to be major creditor of banks, and finally, due to concerns of systemic
risk. In reality the process is still protracted, the Central Bank is no longer the major creditor of
the system, and its institutional knowledge is less relevant than other considerations for asset
recovery. Extra-judicial liquidations of failed banks have proven to be bureaucratic and time
consuming, with significant asset value destruction, burdening the Central Bank with a
responsibility incompatible with its primary function.
104. The Central Bank therefore initiated a thorough scrutiny of the relevant legislation
for bank failure resolution, as well the role of the present deposit insurance scheme; the Fundo
Garantidor de Creditos (FGC), targeted to culminate in the submission to Congress of draft legal
amendments and reforms to FGC statutes. A broad vision of the scope of the review process is
now available. It would assess, inter alias: (i) the reduction of the Central Bank role in the extra-
judicial liquidation process and the increase of the role of the private sector; (ii) the balance of
rules and discretion in the corrective phases of dealing with troubled banks; (iii) the introduction
of more efficient resolution techniques for closed banks-such as "purchase and assumption"
operations; (iv) an enhanced role of FGC in a reformed liquidation process; (v) the strengthening
of FGC financial position, particularly via access to contingent lines of finance; and (vi) possible
changes to the design of the deposit insurance (e.g., the introduction of risk-based premiums and
other complementary monitoring powers).62 An advanced draft of a new law has now been
prepared by a consultant to the Central Bank, although the draft is not yet finalized.
62 Annex 5 to the documentation for PFSECAL1 contains a more detailed discussion of these issues.
Page 38

subject to both subjective (wrong-doing) and objective (even without wrong-doing) responsibility, making
them liable witnhtheir personal assets in the evenL of a bank failure. Proposals under consideration would limit
objective responsibility to owners. Further, there are concerns about the liability of the- liquidator. Since FGC
would be the responsible party and since it is financed by contribution of its member banks, the restriction or
elimination of the liability of the liquidator are also. under'consideration- .'          .

105.   Two initial drafts of new     legislation, had been prepared' by end-2001, one by a
Central Bank staff and another by the FGC, in collaboration with the bank association
FEBRABAN, have been completed and serve as basis for further discussion. Both are now
under review by a high-level financial system attorney who has been contracted by the
Central Bank, and expects to present a draft law by May 2002. Recent laws passed by other
countries adopting "best practices" for bank resolution are being provided to the Central Bank by
the Bank for reference. Details of some of the proposals under consideration today are discussed
in the box below.
The Deposit Insurance Fund - FGC
106.   As noted in the documentation for the first PFSECAL, Brazil's privately run deposit
insurance fund, while enjoying many good structural and governance features, needs to increase
contingent access to liquid private sector resources to confront failures in the segment of larger
banks. In 2001, the deposit insurance institution (Fundo Garantidor de Creditos, FGC)
began to strengthen its efforts to obtain private contingent financing, so that it could lower
Page 39



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
current contributions by its member banks. Further, FGC management has proposed
changes to its statutes that would broaden the financing options and give more
responsibility to management. Revisions of the Monetary Council Resolutions that govern
FGC has been prepared in draft by FGC and these drafts are now under review by the Central
Bank, and will then be voted in an Assembly of Banks.63 It proposes a broadening of its
financing options to include private, public, and multilateral financing. It also aims to reduce its
target assets, currently at 5 percent of all covered deposits, to two percent, which would allow a
lowering of the premium below the current 0.3 percent of all covered deposits. Further,
contingent financing would be included in this 2 percent target. FGC is also asking for
permission to change its member contribution rate without having to go to the Monetary Council,
but in consultation with the Central Bank and the FGC Board. The responsibilities of FGC
management vis-h-vis its Administrative Council would be strengthened, implying hiring of at
least one more executive director, in addition to the sole present director. It is also proposed that
the executive directors would assume objective responsibility for their actions, instead of acting
on behalf of the Administrative Council. However FGC is not planning to expand its operational
structure significantly in preparation for taking over a larger role in bank failure resolution - both
liquidation and intervention - as described above. Rather, it plans on contracting liquidators and
interveners, who could be firms, individuals or other banks, on an as-required basis. FGC is
already currently involved in the liquidation of three failed banks. While being liquidated under
the present regime, the process is being interpreted more flexibly and involves greater
participation of FGC. According to FGC management, the first of these three cases could end
shortly, after "only" three years.
107.  On access to contingent funding, FGC management has been in discussion with 11 major
Brazilian banks (both public and private, domestic and foreign) to obtain a stand-by facility of
R$1.2 billion, with no commitment fee, for a period over five years and renewed yearly. If
drawn upon, the interest rate would be the interbank market rate and the loan would be for
around four years. FGC has asked the Central Bank to allow lending banks to attach a zero risk
weight to this loan. Independent of the result of this request, however, the stand-by agreement
will be signed after the General Assembly of FGC and the Monetary Council have approved the
new FGC statutes. In a second phase, FGC management plans to explore possibility of obtaining
stand-by facilities on the international market. The lowering of the target assets to 2 percent
instead of 5 percent of total covered deposits, together with the inclusion of the contingent
financing facility in this target would allow the substantial lowering of the premium from its
current level of 0.3 percent per year to 0.01 percent per year in 2006. The proposal for
simplifying the procedure for requesting annual changes in contributions should facilitate this
reduction.
Contingency Planning
108. The Central Bank had initiated, in early 2001, work to develop a blueprint contingency
plan-to ensure adequate preparedness to deal with early stages of a financial crisis, should one
unexpectedly arise. Since the spelling out of the broad scope of such a plan, at the time of the
63 Resolution 2197 August 1995 deals with the FGC's establishment and Resolution 2211 of the same year details
its statutes.
Page 40



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
presentation to the Bank's board of the first PFSECAL, authorities have advanced with the plan
through the engagement of high-level consultant services, involved with the pioneering of this
concept. Together with the consultants, a basic approach document has been prepared, which
includes Guidelines for Crisis Contingency Planning. The guidelines identify twelve key sources
of systemic risk in Brazil and propose further work around four building blocks to establish an
effective crisis management capacity, dealing with: a) infornation; b) supervisory powers; c)
readiness to act; and d) stress simulation. The latter includes recommendation for analysis and
simulation in eight areas and leads to a Systemic Risk Mapping methodology. The overall
direction and the proposed framework appear to be positive and appropriate, As such, intensive
technical work on the Contingency Plan had been planned for 2003 (under the Bank-financed
FSTAL), although there is now a possibility that this could be brought forward. Crucial
implementation steps as visualized by the Central Bank include: identifying a group of suitable
individuals who would lead contingency planning; consolidating the advances in offsite
surveillance that already enable the performance of stress simulations; and adopting as
operational the new bank rating system that would be at the center of the Central Bank's
supervisory activities. Finally, proposed changes in enforcement powers as spelled out in the
Central Bank Law currently under preparation are also necessary to support contingency
planning as part of the overall changes in banking supervision.
SECURMTiES MARKETS
109.  Brazil's capital markets performance in 2001 reflected the macroeconomic uncertainties
facing the country, and especially, turbulence in the US and overseas markets from September.
Early optimism in 2001, following a year of good macroeconomic performance, was reflected in
a boost of the BOVESPA stock index by almost 16 percent in January alone (from 15,260 to
17,672) but this soon faded first due to the domestic energy crisis and then the decline in
overseas markets and investor confidence. The index reached a low towards the end of
September at 10,005 on Sep 26, down over 30 percent compared to the start of the year.
Although there was a subsequent year end rally, with calmer intemational markets and positive
national indicators, the market ended 11 percent down over the year as a whole. Trading volume
also declined over the year, with an aggregate fall of 18.8 percent in total turnover and a 2.4
percent decline in market capitalization. Despite 36 new registrations of companies on the
BOVESPA exchange, mostly due to consolidations, restructurings or buybacks, there were also
52 withdrawals, reducing the overall number of public companies by 16, and the number of
listed companies traded on the exchange by thirty-one (428 down from 459).
110.  Yet, in regulatory terms landmark advances were made over this period. As noted in the
documentation for the first PFSECAL, deficiencies in corporate governance, which leave
minority shareholders unduly exposed to risks of expropriation by controlling shareholders have
been a major obstacle to the development of Brazil's securities markets.64 The passage of a

controlling shareholder in the event of a change in corporate control). Other problems are the limited voting shares
and even more limited trading of voting shares Practically the entire "public float" (the set of shares traded) consists
of non-voting shares.

113.   CVM   has a large agenda for the issue of reinforcing implementing regulations for the
new corporate law, and on other themes, for the year ahead. Their issue has awaited the passage
of the revisions of the Corporate law and CVM law, so that they could be consistent with the
anticipated new legal framework. As noted above, CVM's regulatory role is anticipated to have a
major impact on the implementation of the new Corporate Law. From the end of 2001, the issue
of such regulations by CVM accelerated. CVM has already issued Instruction No. 358 (January
3, 2002) which regulates the disclosure of securities related material information. and Instruction
361 (March 5, 2002) concerning tender offers. This Instruction will regulate some of the new
provisions of the Corporate Law, such as the mandatory tender offer in the case of sale of the
corporate control, and presents some significant improvements in this area. With regard to new
regulations on public offerings, including prospectuses, CVM Commissioners are currently
discussing an initial internal draft. Several other Instructions are being prepared, some of which
have already been submitted to the CVM's Commissioners for comments, such as a new
regulation on broker-dealers, which will also apply to derivatives broker-dealers. Parallel to this,
the CVM is preparing, at its highest levels, a Corporate Governance code. An initial draft has
already been prepared. Reforms are also being considered in the area of regulation of rating
agencies.
114.   With regard to the regulation of mutual funds, a major change has been realized through
the passage of new laws; finally, the CVM has been awarded the responsibility for
jurisdiction over all mutual funds, both debt funds and equity funds.69 The CVM and the
Central Bank are jointly reviewing the practical implications of bringing all mutual funds under
CVM's regulation, i.e., CVM's ability, in view of its resource constraints, to cope with this
challenge. Once implemented this would represent a significant strengthening of regulation in
the medium term, and has been remarkably achieved without the need for the passage of a
specific law, as was expected a year ago. It was also expected, a year ago, that a new draft
"Central Bank/Capital Markets" law would also formalize the realignment of regulatory
responsibilities for pension funds, thus comprehensively reorganizing supervision between the
Securities Commission, the Central Bank and other regulatory agencies (referred to as the
proposed Central Bank/Financial Institutions Law). However, it is now proposed that the
merger of the regulation of closed and open ended pension funds - the SPC and the SUSEP

requirements for segmenting the presentation of profits by area of activity. This proposed bill also includes a
provision for the publication of the financial statements of large companies, and the need for compliance with
CVM's accounting and disclosure requirements, whether or not listed. There is a possibility that it could be voted
upon before end-June. In addition, the government is pursuing further accounting and auditing reforms on a broad
front, through new accounting reforms for financial institutions, under the Central Bank, and also through the CVM
and the Ministry of Finance. Meanwhile, the Bank and IMF are undertaking a ROSC on accounting and auditing in
Brazil, under an ongoing FSAP, which will provide timely input on these issues.
69 Although there is no specific article in the revised laws on this, it is implied by the definition of the 'securities'
which CVM is responsible for overseeing, in the revised CVM law.

- will take place in the present year through an executive order, probably by decree. Taken
together, these measures would imply that the objectives of a major anticipated legal change, the
passage of a new law on financial institutions, has effectively been achieved.
115.  Also in the area of pension funds, the creation of new defined contribution pension funds
for government employees is also now envisaged. A new measure has recently been passed,
which requires pension funds to match the duration of their assets and liabilities, thus
creating an increased demand for long term paper such as securitized mortgages and long-
term government indexed paper. Meanwhile new requirements for the marking to market
of securities portfolios and their division into hold and trade categories will render the
operations of pension funds more transparent and contribute to increased financial
soundness.70 Another new regulation strengthening pension fund governance has also been
issued by the Conselho de Gestao da Previdencia Complementar (SPC) which demands that
pension funds representatives disclose the content and the justification of their votes in
shareholders' meetings of corporations in which pension funds holds interests.71 Together
these measures would represent major advances in the area of contractual savings.
116.  Meanwhile, CVM has issued new Instructions regulating mutual funds for asset backed
securities (Instruction 356 of December 17, 2001 on the FIDC) and another on mutual funds for
indexed assets, which have been formally permitted for the first time in 2002 (Instruction 359 of
January 22, 2001).
