Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
117. Strong efforts had been made around a year ago (December 2000) by BOVESPA,
Brazil's stock exchange, to support good governance through the setting up of the Novo
Mercado, particularly designed to attract new corporate listings or IPOs which follow good
governance standards and through the parallel designation of different levels of good governance
for existing listed companies.72 These efforts have made limited progress so far. By end 2001,
only nineteen companies had enrolled as Level 1 (the less stringent level) companies, and no
existing companies had progressed to Level 2. And the first listing on the Novo Mercado
occurred on February 1, 2002.73 However, this was also the first IPO in Brazil since May 2000.
Poor macro and market conditions have certainly been a large factor in the limited success so far
of these measures. BOVESPA is optimistic about further progress on Novo Mercado listings,
and on listings under the two good governance levels, by April 2002. BOVESPA's IGC index, an
index of the good governance companies, has shown an increasing spread over its all-share
index, the IBOVESPA, over the past year.74 As for BNDESpar, some incentives of lower
funding costs have been introduced for companies which want to increase transparency. With
regard to its investment in new private equity funds, increased investment is offered to those
companies which agree to eventually go public in the Novo Mercado. However, given that exit
from these companies will take some years, the impact on the market is difficult to gauge today.
THE PAYMENTS SYSTEM
118.   To summarize the description of the Central Bank's ambitious program for redesigning
Brazil's payment's system infrastructure, the core of the program encompasses a series of actions
aimed at eliminating the risks incurred by the Central Bank, and at transferring residual risks to
relevant private participants in the payments system under new rules and oversight.75 The legal
framework for reforms was established by provisional Decree Law 2008, issued in December
1998, and subsequently modified and reissued as Law 10214 of March 27, 2001. The law clearly
conferred on the Central Bank the oversight responsibility for the payments system while
establishing the framework for defining the rights and responsibilities of private participants in
the payments process. Based upon this legal framework, the Central Bank is far advanced with
the installation of a new settlement system (Sistema de Transferencia de Reservas - STR), which
will settle in real time and on a gross basis transfers of funds on bank reserve accounts - 'real
time gross settlement' (RTGS), which will achieve the objective of eliminating Central Bank
risk, since payments will only be made if there are positive and sufficient balances in the reserve
account to be debited. This system is consistent with best international practice.
72 For details on BOVESPA's Novo Mercado, and its codes of governance, go to http://www.bovespa.com.br/.
Companies already listed on Bovespa are of course allowed to migrate to the Novo Mercado if they follow its
requirements. Three companies have already published material information about their proposed migration to Novo
Mercado including one for Level 2 (Petrobras), and at least another three are preparing for adhesion to Level 1.
73 CCR, Cia. de Concessoes Rodovi6rias, a listing of a basket of toll road concessions.
74 In June 2001, the two indices both stood at around 1000; by end-January 2002, the IGC was at almost 1050 while
the IBOVESPA was just above the 950 mark.
75 World Bank Report No. P7448-BR; April 26, 2001, on the First Programmatic Financial Sector Adjustment
Loan, Annex 7, has details on the payments system reform. For an update, see Annex 4 to the present document.
Meanwhile, a ROSC on Brazil's payments systems currently underway in the FSAP will likely validate the
compliance of the present system with CPSS principles.
Page 46



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
119. Recent Update on Payment System Reform From the time of the launching of the
payments system reform program, the scheduled official date for the new STR system was
announced by the Central Bank to be October 2001. However in September 2001 the Central
Bank announced that the final launch of the new Brazilian large value payments system would
be postponed from October, 2001 to April 22, 2002. The reasons indicated were lack of
readiness of the ten largest commercial banks as well as the several clearinghouses which will
integrate the new system. Meanwhile, the Central Bank also suffered equipment delivery delays.
The new timetable was defined in Circular 3060 of the Central Bank, dated September 20,
2001, which also set a timetable for interim tests. Delays are not surprising; a Bank mission had
earlier commented on the ambitious goals previously announced, possibly in part to spur on
complementary actions required in private participants. The new date was determined in concert
with major private participants, through consultations with the Banker's Association,
FEBRABAN, and was realistic, as shown by its achievement on the target date. Circular 3059
also of September 20, 2001 provides that all securities managed by the CETIP will also have to
be settled on the same day of their maturity or of the maturity of their financial rights (dividends,
interests, etc.).
120.  Meanwhile Brazil continued to take steps towards successively completing the definition
of the regulatory framework within which the new system will operate. Circular 3032 of May
9, 2001 provided for the monitoring of reserve accounts of banks at the BCB. Resolution 2882
of August 30, 2001 dealt with broad principles for risk management at clearing houses. It
specified nine general rules which payments system operators must comply with; rules that
resemble very closely the CPSS Core Principles for Systemically Important Payments System of
the BIS. Circular 3057 of August 31, 2001 approved the detailed regulation of the functioning
of clearinghouses and other payment system operators and defined several features which these
entities should present in terms of capital requirements, transparency, risk control measures,
operational requirements, etc. It also established a formula to determine whether a system is
systemically important, based on the average value of the largest transaction and-or the
aggregate value, both over a time span. Additionally, the Central bank also took proactive
measures to eliminate risks inherent in the check clearinghouse by incentives to drastically
reduce the amount of large value items. A threshold of R$5,000 was identified through
simulations and estimates of average daily clearing house balances and the Central Bank put in
place a mechanism of unremunerated collateralized pre-funding for all checks above this value.
121. Additional measures have been taken which even if not directly associated with the
payments system reform, are likely to impact positively upon its smooth operation On July 26,
2001, the National Monetary Council enacted Resolution 2878 on transparency in financial
transactions, which is known through international experience to strongly benefit efficient
development of a country's payments system. And since June 2001 a new system for handling
suspect banknotes is in place. Other Circulars relating to payments system issues are under
consultation. Among them is a circular to provide access to reserve accounts at the Central Bank
to investment banks and similar financial institutions, and also a circular to redefine rediscount
procedures.
Page 47



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
V. THE PROPOSED LOAN
122.  Programmatic adjustment lending for the financial sector was included in the most recent
CAS progress report (Report 22116-BR discussed on May 24, 2001), and its objective of
strengthening the framework for accelerated and systemically sound growth is an essential part
of Bank assistance for renewed broad-based economic growth and thus poverty reduction. The
proposed Single Tranche US$404.04 million Second Progranunatic Financial Sector
Adjustment Loan is the second in a series of programmatic loans for the financial sector of
Brazil, and follows a First Programmatic Financial Sector Adjustment Loan, which was
approved by the Bank's Board in May 2001, and a Financial Sector Technical Assistance
Loan, approved on September 4,2001.
123.  Brazil has show strong commitment to the maintenance of its comprehensive and
ambitious financial sector reform path over the past year, despite difficult macroeconomic
circumstances, exceeding expectations in many areas, and with an acceleration of structural
change in some of the most critical and difficult areas. Authorities have progressed steadily
towards taking all steps envisaged within the program, to increase the efriciency of
financial intermediation and broadening access to financial services, in strengthening
banking supervision and resolution systems, in progressing with payments systems
reforms, and in reducing barriers to more broad based participation in securities' markets.
In addition, particularly notable are its bold steps towards recognizing liabilities at the
federal banks which form the core of Brazil's financial system and to shield such publicly
owned financial institutions in the future from government mandated losses. There is also a
possibility of fundamental changes in financial sector legislation through the passage of a
Constitutional amendment, which would permit institutional realignment of responsibilities for
financial regulatory institutions. This would also permit the presentation to Congress of a revised
Central Bank law instituting monetary policy independence.
124.  Progress with goals and targets for programmatic reform, as envisaged at the time of the
first loan, as well as additional achievements and targets which constitute pillars of the proposed
second loan, together with expected future reforms, are detailed in Annex 1. The government
has further elaborated its reform program in a Letter of Sectoral Development Policy, transmitted
to the Bank.76 By any standards, the current financial sector reform program envisaged by
Brazil's government is bold and ambitious, and provided expected momentum is maintained, will
be far-reaching and fundamental to Brazil's economic development.
125.  Adjustment lending would support effective and continuing structural reforms to address
the key objectives of fiscal stability and renewed growth and would contribute to Brazil's
external financing requirements of US$47 billion and its nominal public sector deficit of 3.4
percent of GDP in 2002. About US$4.8 billion of this is expected to be met by public sector
lending including multilateral disbursements, and the proposed Second Programmatic Financial
Sector Adjustment Loan, together with the US$450 million FY02 Energy Sector Adjustment
Loan would together remain under the adjustment lending ceiling foreseen by the CAS. Another
Programmatic Fiscal Adjustment Loan could be proposed in FY03.
76 The letter will be made publicly available by the Government when the Government submits the proposed Loan
to the Brazilian Senate for approval.
Page 48



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
126.  On the basis of its importance for growth and poverty reduction, and given the evidence
of reform progress, the Government and the Bank have reconfirmed the financial sector as a
priority area for assistance through programmatic adjustment lending. Programmatic lending
for the financial sector was proposed for a total amount of up to US$1.2 billion, in FY01,
over two to three operations, depending on the progress of reform. Of this sum, $404.04
million has already been disbursed for a first, FY01 operation. The present second loan is
proposed for a similar amount of another US$404.04 million. Programmatic lending is
envisaged to include a possible third additional loan, which would span the period of transition
following the October 2002 elections and thus anchor reforms achieved so far, and provide a
vehicle for dialogue with the next administration.
127.  The first programmatic loan has clearly demonstrated the suitability of the proposed
programmatic lending vehicle for the proposed financial sector adjustment operation. The
programmatic approach was considered particularly suitable due to the difficulty of prediction of
core actions subject to politically sensitive legislative changes. As in the case of the first
operation, the proposed Second Programmatic Loan is in direct support of actions already
completed, and comprises a blend of substantial progress with actions expected at the time
of the First Loan, and additional difficult reforms whose timing was difficult to envisage
only a year ago.
128.  Due to the unpredictability, only a year ago, of the likely pace of reforms of federal
banks, and uncertainties regarding a number of legislative changes, such reforms had been left
largely outside the programmatic sphere of the First Loan. The flexibility afforded by the
programmatic adjustment framework permits the present operation to support and partner recent
and significant progress achieved in reform areas deemed to be outside the first adjustment
operation, while simultaneously acknowledging excellent progress with meeting, and in many
cases exceeding, virtually all expected reform landmarks as envisaged by the first operation. The
combination of these two broad groups of elements forms the basis for the present operation.
With the unexpected acceleration of reforms in areas previously deemed to be
unpredictable and sensitive, and the opening up of government dialogue with the Bank on
these reform areas, particularly public bank reform, the present operation extends the
frontiers of the Bank supported program to a substantially larger range of the
Government's overall financial sector reform agenda. (See Annex 1 for details).
129.  The series of programmatic adjustment operations to Brazil's financial sector have been,
and continue to be, supported by an extensive partnership based on analytical and advisory
work (AAA), technical assistance lending and continuous dialogue at the highest levels. The
backbone of this partnership was originally the Bank's first technical assistance loan to the
Central Bank, which had a major emphasis on banking regulation and supervision (Loan BR-
4245 of 1997), and which also provided flexibly for support for the modernization of the Central
Bank in a range of other areas. Work launched through this loan on the strengthening of bank
supervision contributed to the issuing of a series of prudential regulations to safeguard banking
system soundness, and also to the program of onsite-supervision referred to as the Consolidated
Global Inspections, which were applied for the first time to Federal banks in 1999-2000. The
present program of Federal bank balance sheet restructuring has its underpinnings in the
application on the basis of inspection reports of recently issued prudential regulations, which the
Federal Banks are now required to be in compliance with. Themes included in the first
Page 49



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
programmatic loan, and continued in the second, on orderly bank failure resolution and on the
strengthening of the were first discussed with the government by the Bank in 1998, in the context
of the preparation of a Special Financial Sector Adjustment Loan.
130.  Over the 1999-2000 period, as noted in the documentation for the first programmatic
financial sector loan, exchanges and policy discussion on Brazil's financial system with the Bank
grew more extensive and exploratory in scope, expanding and deepening to encompass a number
of jointly selected new areas, through a series of FY00 targeted policy notes, on the overall
efficiency of financial intermediation ("Impediments to the Development and Efficiency of
Financial Intermediation in Brazil"), regulatory issues ("Optimal Regulatory and Supervisory
Structures: Economic Issues"), debt management and debt markets, as well as more
comprehensive study on capital markets ("Corporate Governance Reform Issues in the Brazilian
Equities Markets").  Additionally, as part of a multi-country Western Hemisphere project, a
detailed study was completed on payments systems and securities clearance and settlement. The
dialogue also included municipal finance, as well as pension reform, also supported by both
lending and ESW. Issues concerning poverty and the financial sector were first approached, and
initially tackled through a hands-on involvement by the Bank, in the form of a microfinance
project (CrediAmigo; Loan No. 4554) which has proven to be very successful.
131.  Further new areas of joint exploration have begun in 2001. FY02 began with the
presentation to the Bank's Board of a second Technical Assistance loan (Loan No. 4637-BR) for
Brazil's financial sector, which this time partners Brazil's Securities Commission, the CVM, in
addition to the Central Bank. Intended to support the implementation of programmatic lending,
as well as to build capacity in the two institutions for the implementation of their mandates, the
new technical assistance loan considerably extends the frontiers of the Bank's engagement in
Brazil's financial sector. The second major area of collaboration is on finance and poverty, which
has been launched in FY02 though a major study, undertaken at the request of and in
collaboration with the Central Bank of Brazil, on Access to Financial Services. The study has
received strong support as well as funding from the Bank's financial sector network and is the
most ambitious of its kind to be undertaken so far in the Bank. It includes an investigation of
overall impediments to the expansion of microfinance in Brazil, an exploration of the potential
for the 'downscaling' of private and commercial bank lending to smaller and poorer borrowers;
evaluations of public policies for access, many of which operate through the large federal banks,
and infrastructure impediments, including credit information, efficiency of small value
payments, and related themes. Examinations of rural finance and housing finance are part of the
agenda. The work on housing finance involves an examination of the operations of the present
system, currently dominated by the largest of Brazil's Federal banks; the Caixa Economica
Federal, which has not only been cooperative but solicitous of Bank inputs and suggestions for
the strengthening of the housing finance system.
REFORM PROGRAM SUPPORTED BY THE BANK
132. The status of the overall Programmatic Reform, covering actions completed in the
currently proposed Second phase, actions achieved in the First phase, as well as possible future
77 The major papers were reviewed in FYO1 by the Quality Assurance Group and received favorable comments.
Page 50



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
actions for a potential Third programmatic phase, is shown in Annex 1. Details of the present
proposed second operation are discussed below, both in the context of expectations at the onset
of financial sector programmatic lending, as well as in view of the rapid evolution of sectoral
reforms over the last twelve month. Possible future actions, in addition to those below, could also
be expanded by the joint Bank-Fund FSAP (financial sector assessment program) currently under
way in Brazil.
Progress on Targets under the First Programmatic Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
133.  Reforms supported by the first programmatic loan comprised actions to (i) raise
efficiency in financial intermediation, reduce intermediation costs and broaden access; (ii)
promote the soundness of the banking system and its defenses against financial crisis; (iii)
enhance transparency, promoting good governance, and strengthening the regulator in securities
markets; and (iv) protect the safety and soundness of the financial system through payments
systems reforms. Broadly speaking, targets envisaged by the first loan have been met or
exceeded in virtually all areas, as revealed in the financial sector update in Part IV. Within these
broad areas, key specific elements supported under the first loan, actions envisaged for
subsequent programmatic lending and their status of achievement, and hence, actions supported
by the proposed Second Programmatic Adjustment operation are detailed below. Actions which
could be envisaged for a possible third phase operation are also discussed. Broadly speaking,
targets envisaged by the first loan have been met or exceeded in virtually all areas, as revealed in
the financial sector update in Part IV.
134.  Intermediation Eficiency and Access to Financial Services: With respect to high
financial intermediation spreads, actions supported under the First Loan included increased
disclosure of debtor information by the Central Bank Risk Center and improved credit
enforcement through the creation of a new lending contract (the Cedula de Credito Bancdrio),
and the submission to Congress of new legislation to overhaul bankruptcy laws. Core indicative
actions for a second phase included wide availability of enhanced debtor information, and
confirmation by law of the new "Cedula" instrument. In terms of achievements, supported by
the proposed Second Programmatic Loan, the Risk Center is now producing considerably
enhanced information, on an extended range of small value loans, and encompassing a range of
micro institutions not hitherto included. A contract has been signed, and work has been launched
for a further phase. The Cedula now has the status of a legal instrument, and has been extended
in terms of application, beyond expectations. Additional indicative actions including studies on
taxation and the preparation of new draft legislation on bankruptcy and bank failure resolution
are ongoing. Overall progress is therefore deemed to be very satisfactory. Core indicative
action envisaged today for a Third phase could include a review of limitations on information
sharing under the new Risk Center, and, as foreseen earlier, the passage through Congress of a
new bankruptcy law. With regard to taxation of financial services, as planned, assessments of the
impact of the CPMF had been made which reveal its adverse impact on the financial system.
135. Broadened access to financial services was supported in the First loan through
regulatory steps taken to extend banking service by authorizing banks to use locations other than
branches, and reducing restrictive membership rules for cooperatives. Indicative Actions
anticipated for the Second and Third phases of programmatic lending focused on the
formulation of a strategy and action plan to further expand financial services, including through
Page 51



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
the collateralization of credit. Achievements to date, supported by the proposed Second
Programmatic Loan, include the setting up of a high level investigative committee on
microfinance which has produced detailed Action Plans on the expansion of microcredit,
collaboration in a broad ranging Bank study on access to financial services, the government's
auction of the franchise of post offices to financial institutions, for the extension of the network
of provision of financial services, the programs being offered by SEBRAE to microcredit
institutions, and the initiation of sales of retail government bonds to individual savers.
Expectations in this area have not only been met but exceeded, and Bank dialogue in this
area has intensified. In a Third phase, the govemment could adopt further measures to expand
the role of microcredit or other forms of private finance, while rationalizing the role of
govemment and of federal banks in supporting access.
136. Bank System Soundness and Safety Net: The First programmatic loan supported bank
regulation/supervision reforms including the introduction of consolidated supervision of
financial conglomerates, strengthening of capital adequacy standards, creation of a sound system
of asset classification that supports more rigorous provisioning rules, major organizational
streamlining within the supervision department of the Central Bank, progress in completing new
examination manuals and initiation of a new bank rating system. A review program of the bank
exit framework and the role of the deposit insurance was also supported and a decision was
reached to begin work on a contingency plan for bank crises. Core actions anticipated for a
Second phase included the introduction of examination manuals and a bank rating system and
submission to Congress of a law to better protect bank supervisors, together with submission for
approval of draft legislation on bank resolution as well as new draft statutes for the deposit
insurer. Approval of a contingency plan was also anticipated.
137.  Achievements in these areas, which constitute actions supported by the Second
Programmatic Loan, demonstrate sustained progress in strengthening banking supervision. All
anticipated projects under the Banking supervision superintendency are underway and are
expected to be complete within the year. Despite an enhancement in scope of work, new
examination manuals are expected to be completed by August 2002, and a new offsite
surveillance system was completed at the end of 2001 and is now operational. After some early
delays, contracts for the further extension of the Credit Risk Center have been approved and
work has been initiated and is proceeding well. The completion of this phase of extension is
anticipated to be around November 2002. Meanwhile regulations have been issued extending the
scope of institutions which are required to submit data to this Center. Work has also been
initiated on the design and introduction of a new bank rating system, which is expected to be
completed by July 2002. Progress in new regulatory reforms in areas such as accounting were
not anticipated and are welcome additions to the proposed program.
138.  One hoped for action is undoubtedly falling behind and this is the presentation to
Congress of a law to better protect supervisors. Despite strong backing from the Central Bank,
political opposition has been encountered which would make it difficult, and indeed largely
fruitless at the present juncture, to present such a proposal to Congress. As such, delays in
submission are disappointing but not altogether surprising to Bank staff. Viewed within the
larger picture, however, this does not dilute the overall judgment of substantial fulfillment of
program goals in the area of the strengthening of bank supervision. Anticipated core actions for a
Third Phase are the effective operation of the new off-site surveillance system and its generation
Page 52



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
of simulations, reports and stress tests, as well as the application of examination manuals and the
new bank rating system to the supervision process. The proposed draft Central Bank law could
also be a vehicle to afford some protection to bank supervisors. These issues could be discussed
and agreed with the new administration in CY03.
139.  Regarding bank resolution and the safety net, high level consultancy services have
been contracted by the Central Bank for the complex review of the bank exit framework and the
preparation of draft new legislation in this area. In parallel, the deposit insurance agency, FGC,
has also reviewed its statutes and has proposed recommendations for their strengthening and
modification, for incorporation in a proposed new resolution of the National Monetary Council.
140.  The Central Bank has also prepared an initial blueprint for contingency crisis planning,
with the support of suitable international experts, which has been favorably reviewed by the
Bank. In sum, there is steady and very satisfactory progress on all fronts with regards to
actions envisaged for the strengthening of supervision and bank failure resolution. Delays
of a few months are acknowledged with regard to the further enhancement of the Credit Risk
Center and the introduction of the bank rating system, and work is well under way. A longer
delay is anticipated with regard to the submission to Congress of draft new legislation for bank
failure resolution and bank exit, and this is largely due to the extreme complexity of the task, and
the inclusion in its ambit of consideration the roles for several different players, including the
judiciary. Delays in the submission of early proposals are partially due to the recognition of
imperfections and consequent discussions of new drafts. While this necessitates a partial return
to the drawing board, it is likely to lead to sounder proposals, which have been more thoroughly
reviewed and debated, in the long term. Finally, core actions for a Third phase could include
publication of new laws for the bank exit framework and new deposit insurance statutes. Further
formal progress on the contingency plan, although envisaged in the First Loan, is not a core
action for the third phase, given its time sequencing, which requires that certain actions are
completed (e.g., the bank rating system, offsite surveillance, and protection to supervisors)
before much progress can be made.
141. Payments and Securities Clearance and Settlement Systems: The First programmatic
loan supported the launch of landmark reforms in Brazil's payments system, aimed at first,
reducing systemic risk and Central Bank exposure to loss in the settlement of payments, and
second, ensuring the prudent management of residual risks by private participants in the clearing
process, was recognized and by the first programmatic loan. Core actions for the Second phase
targeted the implementation and functioning of the new payment system and the issue of the
guidelines for risk management at private clearing houses. In terms of achievements, the Second
Loan will support first of all the launching of the new payments system. While some delays
have occurred in its full operationalization, these were not unexpected in view of the ambitious
initial launch schedule of October 2001 announced by the Central bank, partly with a view to
motivate and energize participant private banks. The revised launch date, set at April 22, 2002,
was achieved. The new date was determined in September 2001, and for the first time enjoyed
the consensus and support of the private banks, through a formal agreement with FEBRABAN,
the National Association of Banks. The Second Loan also supports the issue of a series of
additional regulations which clarify the legal framework in which the new system will
operate, notably Circular 3057 of August 31, 2001, which approves statues of clearing
houses, and Resolution 2882 of August 30, 2001 which deals with broad principles for risk
Page 53



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
management at clearing houses. Future reforms in this area for a third loan could include
evidence of the full and satisfactory functioning of the new payments system, and satisfactory
operations of clearing houses, with special attention to risk management.
142. Securities Markets: The first loan supported Brazil's progress in modernizing corporate
governance and in the regulatory framework and enforcement, including the submission to
Congress of the Corporate Law, and the issuance of good govemance guidelines by the stock
exchange, BNDESPAR (equity investment subsidiary of Brazil's National Development Bank)
and the pension fund regulator. The second programmatic phase envisaged support for the
approval of the revised Corporate and CVM laws, the issue of additional regulations to perfect
and consolidate minority shareholder protection, and submission to Congress of a new Central
Bank/Financial Systems law to develop an effective securities' market regulatory structure. In
terns of achievements, the landmark passage of the Corporate law has now taken place
and it will be effective from March 1, 2002. This may be regarded as progress with
fundamental financial system legislation. Moreover, proposed amendments of the CVM
law enhancing its enforcement capacity have also been approved, and a revised CVM law
was issued in February 2002.
143. The passage of the Corporate Law and revisions to the CVM law has now accelerated the
pace of issue of accompanying regulations to the new law, to consolidate new principles of
governance. A first CVM Instruction on disclosure of material information was issued early this
year (No. 358 of January 3, 2002); followed swiftly by another comprehensive regulation on
tender offers which will lend protection to minority shareholders (No. 361 of March 5, 2002).
There is an impressive agenda of further regulations that the CVM is now in the process of
issuing, which will provide the practical guidelines for the implementation of governance
changes. The second loan supports the progress made by the CVM in the issue of
regulations enhancing good governance and protecting minority shareholders. Core actions
for a Third phase could include the completion of CVM's program of issue of regulations to
accompany the new corporate law, as well as the undertaking by CVM and BOVESPA of an
assessment of the impact of governance changes. Finally, the second operation also supports
the legal achievement of the consolidation of mutual fund oversight (hitherto divided
between the Central Bank and the CVM) under the CVM (though modifications to the
CVM law), and the passage of regulations which strengthen the financial soundness and
governance of pension funds. It is noted also that the consolidation of pension fund regulation
under the SUSEP is also imminent and expected to occur by executive order before year end.
These represent major steps forward in the rationalization of the overall environment for
financial system regulation, achieved without the need for the submission of a Central Bank /
financial institutions law.
Public Bank Reform
144.  This area was not within the scope of the first Loan, due to unpredictability at that
juncture of likely progress in this area, and limited Bank dialogue. Together with the launching
of federal bank reform, there has been an elevation and expansion in Bank dialogue with
authorities in Brazil, to include a discussion and detailed examination of these issues. The
present operation first supports measures to increase efficiency and transparency in the
public banks and to clearly separate on paper their relations with the government.
Page 54



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
Specifically, the operation seeks to support the first phase of federal bank restructuring, through
(i) Removal of credit risk from the operations funded by the so called "Constitutional Funds"
managed by these banks prior to November 30, 1998; (ii) Agreement to the principle that new
loans from "Constitutional Funds" and other special purpose development funds managed by the
banks will be undertaken with a recognition of the risks entailed. Federal banks can now decide
whether or not they wish to share the credit risk of such loans, receiving higher returns if they
agree to bear such risks;78 (iii) Authorization to the Government to void guarantees given by the
federal banks for rural credits sold to the Government at book value. Thus these banks will not
bear any further responsibility for credit risk on large volumes of old, nonperforrning rural and
real estate loans, which have been swapped with the government for new, negotiable, debt;79 (iv)
Authorization to the government to net out the debit and credit accounts of the federal banks
with the Federation; and finally, (v) Establishing special debt-for-bond swap programs for
various programs/debts held by each of the four federal banks.
145.   In addition, the proposed operation supports the preparation of a blueprint for a time
bound and monitorable action plans for future proposed phases of federal bank reform,
which could help to consolidate the benefits of financial restructuring. Its key features
'include (i) Establishing a framework of accountability with decentralized reporting, providing
for more objective and commercial decision making; (ii) Developing a new commercial
strategy and new products to diversify away from their traditional targeted sectors and
Government-oriented programs; (iii) Organizing activities by major business lines and
separating out Government-related activities; (iv) Improving management information
systems to support the monitoring of the above actions and to view the performance of each
major business line, especially for Government programs, hence enabling performance
monitoring on a risk adjusted basis, and finally, (v) Continued strong supervision,
benchmarking, disclosure and internal transparency of the federal banks. A third operation
could be based on the adoption and execution of such a program.
Fundamental Financial System Legislation
146.   Recognizing progress with the passage of fundamental financial system legislation, core
actions supported by the Second Programmatic Loan are first, the landmark passage of the
Corporate Law and revisions to the Law for the Securities Commission - the CVM law. In
addition, the program recognizes the importance of Constitutional Amendment 32, which
enables the effective conversion into law of many financial and economic measures previously
uncertain, due to the need for their periodic renewal. These include particularly the effective
voiding of the usury law for financial institutions, and the new binding status of the Cedula
instruments; both the Cedula do Cridito Bancdrio and the Cedula do Credito Imobili4rio.
Finally, should the proposed Constitutional Amendment No. 192 achieve passage before year

option (ii) the bank only assumes 50 percent of the credit risk, receives a lower return (3 percent), and cannot deem
funds received to be part of its Tier 2 capital. The main beneficiary of the first option is likely to be Banco do Brasil.

end, it would represent a major unexpected windfall from a policy viewpoint. This is not

series of complementary laws. Closely associated with this is the support under the proposed
program for the presentation to Congress of the draft Central Bank law, which would
institutionalize monetary responsibility.
147.  All the above actions are expected to enable the strengthening of the financial system's
basic regulatory framework, thus increasing its safety and efficiency and promoting crisis-free
growth.
DEscRIPTIoN OF FINANCIAL ASSISTANCE
148. The Bank's financial assistance under this Second programmatic loan follows a first
Single-Tranche Loan disbursed in FY01, and now proposes a Second Single-Tranche Loan. An
additional programmatic loans is envisaged, subject to sustained progress in reform
implementation. Similar to the first loan, the Second Loan, in a proposed amnount of US$404.04
million would be likely to disburse soon after effectiveness, as supported policy actions are
already met prior to Board presentation proposed for June 13, 2002. If there is a third loan, it
could disburse in 2003 or beyond.
149. The Bank's financial assistance will help meet Brazil's external financing requirements.
Brazil's external financing requirements in 2002 are estimated at some US$47 billion, based on a
US$20 billion current account deficit (down from US$27 billion a year ago) and US$27 billion
amortization of medium and long term debt (compared to US$29 billion in the previous year).
The role of foreign direct investment in bridging the gap is somewhat reduced, due to
deteriorating world circumstances, with forecast flows for 2002 of US$16 billion (compared to
flows of US$23 billion for 2001. Around US$4.8 billion is expected to be met by public sector
lending including multilateral disbursements, with the remainder being financed by private sector
rollovers. The proposed Second Programmatic Financial Sector Adjustment Loan is in line with
present CAS ceilings, and is presented in parallel with an FY02 Energy Sector adjustment loan.
A Second Programmatic Fiscal Adjustment could be presented in FY03.
150.  In addition to financing part of balance of payments needs, the loan will help meet the
federal government's financing requirements of about $15 billion (3.4 percent of GDP) in 2002
and will help lengthen the term structure of public sector debt and thus reduce vulnerability. In
the context of current international economic uncertainties and the perception of emerging
market country risk, access to alternative external debt financing for Brazil remains unreliable.
The cost of alternative internal and external debt financing has remained high with recent market
vulnerability, resulting from uncertainties related to problems in neighboring Argentina, and the
economic downturn in the US. Sovereign bond spreads, which stood at lows of around 650 in
February 2001, rose to over 970 by the end of September 2001, and have come down since, but
only to around 870 by February 2002. However, the upgrading of Brazil's sovereign ratings in
March 2002 signaled the decoupling for investors of Brazil's prospects from the fate of
Argentina. Finally, support provided by the Bank, soundly anchored in sustained programmatic
lending and the commitment to and achievement of significant structural reform which is integral
Page 56



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
to such lending, plays a pivotal signaling role at this juncture in terms of building market
confidence in Brazil's continued economic stability, and could also reduce somewhat its overall
external borrowing costs.
151.  Phased programmatic financial sector lending to Brazil has been complemented by a
second companion Financial Sector Technical Assistance Loan, approved by the Bank's Board in
September 2001, in the amount of US$14.4 million, which includes components to address
reform needs of both the Central Bank and the Securities Commission (CVM). Technical
assistance expenditures of both the existing Central Bank TA loan and the second companion TA
loan have also been designed to pave the way for policy reforms targeted for subsequent
programmatic loans and to build capacity for reform implementation. Technical assistance will
be provided to allow for specialized consulting advice in areas which would fortify the
professional capacity of the two regulatory agencies, to further training, to upgrade information
technology, and to allow for diagnostic studies and legal drafting of proposed new policies. At
the Central Bank, in addition to information technology, specific assistance will be given to
areas such as the successful functioning of the new payments system, through diagnostic work
on risk management, and to the deepening of Brazil's debt markets, through an evaluation of
technological options for government securities markets. Within the CVM, technical assistance
would be focused on enabling the staff to update their skills to meet market requirements, for
example in areas such as corporate valuation and accounting, strengthening investor protection,
increasing disclosure and transparency. In addition, information technology needs for data
analysis, for market surveillance and for enhanced disclosure and investor protection would also
be addressed. Certain areas of specialized consulting advice, focused on regulatory issues jointly
shared by the Central Bank and the CVM, could be shared by both institutions.
Program Implementation and Supervision
152.  As over the past year, regular Bank missions will continue to review progress of the
implementation of the proposed reforms and their outcomes. The review will be based on
specific monitoring of reform actions, monitoring indicators and programmatic goals and targets
of the reforms outlined in Annex 1; on the broader overall view of financial sector evolution in
which the Bank and government are jointly engaged on a number of fronts, and on the progress
in implementing TA loan components in support of the reform direction. Finally, future reform
actions indicated in the Letter of Development Policy submitted by the Government to the Bank
will be closely followed. 80

Disbursement, Auditing and Fiduciary Environment
154.  The Loan would disburse under the Bank's provisions for fast disbursing operations,
which require no procurement of goods and services. The flow of proceeds would follow
80 The letter will be made public by the Government in accordance with Brazilian procedures at the time of

procedures now well established under the prior programmatic Financial Sector Adjustment loan,

155.  As discussed in the 2001 CAS Progress Report, and reported in the documentation of the
First Programmatic Financial Sector Adjustment Loan, Brazil has a supportive fiduciary
environment for the proposed operation. Furthermore, the Government is engaged in a
process of strengthening its expenditure review, financial management, procurement and
auditing functions. The Bank has been involved in several of these initiatives.
156.  The Federal Government has over the last years consolidated effective and transparent
expenditure planning, budgeting, and rmancial management systems. These systems include
multi-year planning (Plano Plurianual - PPA), strategic budget planning, the annual law of
budget guidelines, and the budget law itself. The monitoring and evaluation system of the PPA
constitutes a framework for gradually institutionalizing public expenditure reviews that are built
into the regular planning and budgeting cycle.
157. The Brazilian Government and the Bank are finalizing a Country Financial and
Accountability Assessment (CFAA), which reviews the systems and procedures used by the
Government of Brazil at the national level to budget, expend, account for, report on, and audit
the use of funds approved in their annual budget. The report concludes that at the national level,
public financial information is reliable, adequate systems exist to track receipt and use of
funds, and there is a high degree of fiscal transparency. The report notes that the federal
financial management system is among the most effective in the Region. It also raises a number
of areas where further modernization is desirable, including simplification and streamlining of
budget execution processes.
158.  The Government and the Bank have also collaborated in a Country Procurement Issues
Paper (CPIP). This review concluded that while further modernization is recommend in some
areas, the overall framework for public procurement in Brazil is satisfactory, and among the
most robust in the Region. The Government's use of e-procurement is considered best practice.
The CPIP assessment is now being expanded, and the work will be converted into a Country
Procurement Assessment Report (CPAR) in FY03.
159.  Regarding  Bank-financed  projects in  general, a  decentralized  Brasilia-based
implementation team of financial management, procurement and disbursement staff help to
maintain high standards with respect to financial management, procurement, and accountability.
Training of executing agency staff in procurement, financial management, disbursement and
auditing under a recently completed IDF grant has helped to strengthen fiduciary capacity.
Proposed future support to the Brazilian Government in the fiduciary area may include a possible
fiduciary LIL to assist the Government of Brazil in addressing the modernization needs
identified in the fiduciary assessments above, as well as implementation of a program of
financial management and procurement assessments at the state level.
160.  Finally, with regard to the ongoing as well as new technical assistance loans to the
Central Bank and to Brazil's Securities Commission, both institutions have show themselves to
be able to comply with the most stringent of financial management reporting requirements, and
Page 58



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
requests have been made for disbursements under the second TA loan (Financial Sector
Technical Assistance Loan; Loan No. 4637-BR) on the basis of project management reports, a
system which requires sophisticated monitoring and tracking of information in a specialized
format, although potentially easier for the borrower once it is installed. Both agencies involved
have shown themselves to be able to produce the required financial reports for compliance.
ENViRONM ENT
161. Although the financial sector is generally been deemed to have few environmental
issues, a review was nonetheless commissioned of potential environmental considerations,
through an investigation by an independent consultant. Main issues included in the terms of
reference for the background study included (i) a broad investigation of present environmental
policies and standards applicable towards both federal and private bank lending; (ii) issues
concerning the application of such standards, at both federal and private banks; and how these
are taken into consideration for credit decisions; (iii) the possibility of the existence of
environmental liabilities in the portfolio of federal banks, which may require restructuring, and
measures taken to deal with such liabilities.
162.   A detailed report has been produced which is available on file; key points to emerge are
summarized here. An Integrated Safeguards datasheet has been filed. As expected and based
both on the Bank's current guidelines, and on the enhanced information produced in the
consultants report, the project is deemed to have no environmental impact (i.e., a "C" rating is
awarded).
163.  The report points out that broad principles covering issues of bank lending and the
environment were established in Brazil in 1995, under the "Protocol Verde".81 The Protocol
Verde Commission promoted a series of positive actions for the systematic incorporation of
environmental issues in credit procedures at the four federal banks, and has had a substantial and
lasting impact on the incorporation of environmentally sound lending practices at these
institutions. Some observers point out that the work of the commission has wound down in the
last two years. However a detailed diagnostic study currently underway at the MMA (Minist&rio
do Meio Ambiente, dos Recursos Hfdricos e da Amaz6nia Legal) on the Commission's work
points out that the apparent reduction is basically to do with refocusing, and that it should be
viewed as an opportunity for repositioning this work with a new emphasis on market-based
instruments for environmental management. Such instruments would focus on the entire range of
financial instruments, apart from traditional credits, to also include for example environmental
securities and real estate instruments.
81 Through the work of a commission which comprised representatives of the Ministries of Environment,
Agriculture, Finance and Planning and representatives from IBAMA, (a policy institute for the environmental
issues: Instituto Brasileiro do Meio Ambiente e dos Recursos Naturais Renovdveis), the Central Bank, and the five
federal banks; BNDES, BB, CEF, BNB and BASA. Its Letter of Principles for Sustainable Development, which is
based on terms recommended by UNEP (United Nations Environmental Program) came to be known as the
"Protocol Verde", and the working group became a standing Commission subordinated to the Natural Resources
Committee of the Casa Civil from the Presidency of the Republic.

Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
164.  The investigation of environmental practices at individual banks had many positive
findings (see Box); notable among these are the high environmental standards of the BNDES
bank, which in turn are upheld by other banks, as recipients of BNDES lines of credit. Such lines
of credit are extended to both other federal banks as well as to private institutions. Additionally,
Banco do Brasil, the largest bank in Latin America, also federally owned, has not only
systemically instituted sound environmental practices, but also, it has various special programs
with an environmental focus, for example on practices such as energy saving, recycling and the
encouragement of organic cultivation. Caixa Economica Federal, the second largest bank, has
adopted environmental norms which are stricter than those of the National Environmental
Council with regard to parameters such as population density. The incorporation of
environmental training for microcredit loan officers in Banco do Nordeste are considered close
to best practice even by international standards. In the private sector, the IFC's influence on
environmental standards is strong, and awareness is increasing. Bradesco, Brazil's largest private
bank, shows that management of environmental variables can also increase business
opportunities.
165.  Regarding the treatment of environmental liabilities in the process of bank restructuring
or privatization, no major issues were revealed regarding the transfers of such liabilities in the
course of privatization. Bank privatizations so far have been preceded by restructuring processes
and asset sales which would have reduced greatly the possibility of such transfers. Although
there have been no clearly identified environmental liabilities in such restructurings, bank claims
on companies which could have had such issues can be reviewed. In such cases, banks which
were privatized, merged or acquired were divided into a 'good' bank to be incorporated and a
'bad' bank to be liquidated. Potential environmental liabilities were left to the part of the
portfolio destined for liquidation or sale. Thus there are no known pending concerns regarding
environmental liabilities of the institutions either acquired or purchased. In the case of the sale of
Banespa, control of the electricity generating company CHESF (electrical sector), was separated
from the rest of assets prior to sale. Similarly in the case of Unibanco's acquisition of National
Bank (Banco Nacional), the latter detached itself from claims on the Serra da Mesa
(hydroelectric plant) prior to the merger. Looking at strictly private acquisitions, Banco
Econ6mico, absorbed by BBV, had a possible environmental liability; the COPENE
petrochemical industry; and in the case of Bamerindus, bought by HSBC, there could have been
potential environmental liabilities emanating from claims on paper and cellulose sectors. In all
these cases, these assets were separated from the 'good bank' prior to sale.
166.   The report concludes, broadly, that Brazilian environmental legislation has
consolidated itself in the last two decades, so that norms, criteria and environmental
standards specified are of high quality. The greatest fragilities of the Brazilian
environmental system are found in the administrative guardianship of the environment.
Inspection agencies, except in some few states, are unprepared to exercise their function. Norms
and processes for licensing and environmental control at state and municipal levels are
frequently inadequate. However the Environment Ministry is well aware of these weaknesses
and the Bank and the IDB are financing programs looking at corrections.
167.  The issue of what can be done to further environmental standards is complex and
deserves debate and study. Imposing additional standards can be costly, especially for small
Page 61



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
enterprises which rarely have sufficient scale to economically support this. Most of the
environmental credits of the federal banks have been under special government programs,
typically highly subsidized. It can be added that while asset quality information on these loans is
not specifically available, some bad assets are likely to have accumulated, as with other special
programs mandated for these banks, which could have contributed to their financial weaknesses.
The adoption of rigorous environmental standards can complicate the access to credit of small
enterprises and their privileged terms. Also the delegation of licensing to municipalities, NGOs
and others government agencies, would untangle processes, but could diminish the efficiency in
the controls
168.  The report concludes thatfirst steps could be increased participatory public debate
in this area, involving banks, insurers, certifiers, business institutions especially those
sponsored by government such as Senai, Senac, Sesc, Sebrae and others, and government
agencies involved in the environment. A second key step could be an increase in the training
and building of human and institutional capacity to deal with these issues.
169.  As follow up to this report, the Bank team forwarded the consultant study to the banking
system through the offices of FEBRABAN, the bankers association, and also to the Central
Bank. Both are prepared to engage in follow up seminars as recommended and dialogue between
them has begun. A joint working commission, which includes a senior Central Bank Director,
ahs just been established. FEBRABAN has already begun to actively engage in initiatives
concerning sustainable banking. Even before this, in March 2002, FEBRABAN had previosly
organized a debate on environmental risks and opportunities for banks (Riscos e oportunidades
ambientais para bancos), which was held in Sao Paulo on March 6. The keynote speaker was
from IFC. Over 70 persons from different banks attended the event. In March, besides this event,
there was another organized by ABN Amro bank and one by the UNEP in Rio de Janeiro, where
attendance from Brazilian banks was high.
170. The debate of environmental issues and the financial sector continues. The Bank is
following discussions between the government and the private sector exploring the extension of
the Protocol Verde to private banks as well as analyzing proposals such as reforms of the
current environmental licensing system, exploration of the regulation of saleable
environmental securities and insurance against environmental risks and programs for
continued training of human resources, within financial institutions as well as in partner
implementing agencies.
BENEsrrs OF THE PROPOSED LOAN
171.  Brazil's financial sector reform program will help to stimulate as well as firmly anchor
sustainable and sound economic growth and poverty reduction through enhanced protection
against economic turbulence and potential crises, and through its direct support of measures to
enhance access of financial services to the poor. Specifically, the multiple benefits of achieving
programmatic actions as indicated in the first adjustment loan as indicated in the first loan,
include (i) broadened access to financial services and enhanced depth of private financial
intermediation; (ii) sounder operations of both public and private banks and more effective
bank failure resolution and exit; (iii) reduced systemic risk and Central Bank exposure to risk of
Page 62



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
loss in the settlement of payments, and (iv) increased minority shareholder demand for
securities and hence enhanced access to capital for enterprise growth.
172. Expected benefits of public bank reform encompass: enhanced financial soundness in
Brazil's largest financial institutions; movement towards the separation of their commercial
operations from public policy mandates; enhanced fiscal transparency; reduction of distortions in
financial markets and the creation of a more level playing field for all financial institutions, thus
helping overall resource allocation. Until recently, Federal banks were effectively not subject to
even basic prudential norms such as capital adequacy or provisioning, and their real financial
condition was masked. Today their losses are transparent and moreover the government as their
owner has transferred new capital to them to cover old losses due to obligatory operations.
173.  Benefits of progress with fundamental financial sector legislation focus importantly on
the overall rationalization of the roles of Brazil's multiple financial system regulatory
institutions, through the Corporate law, the strengthened CVM, rationalized regulations for
mutual funds and pension funds. Legislative changes to the Corporate law significantly improve
the governance framework for corporations, thus strengthening shareholder rights and
encouraging increased participation in Brazil's stock markets; thus enhancing access to capital
and lowered costs of capital for Brazil's enterprise If it occurs, the institutionalization of
monetary policy independence, and the possibility offurtherfinancial sector rationalization after
the 'unblocking' of Article 192 of the Constitution, would be an added bonus. The ongoing
technical assistance loan to the Central Bank (4254-BR), as well as the new companion
technical assistance loan to the Central Bank as well as the Securities Commission, which went
to the Bank's Board in September 2001 (Loan 4637-BR) will help to fortify institutional capacity
to realize the achievement of the goals of programmatic lending.
174.  Objectives, outcome indicators and poverty impact are summarized in Table 2.

Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
RISKS AND RISK MITIGATION
Political Uncertainty
175.  The comprehensiveness and pace of the reform program so far has been sustained by the
well-coordinated current economic team, working collaboratively across the Central Bank,
Ministry of Finance and regulatory agencies, and the support this team has enjoyed from the
Office of the President of the Republic. The outlook after the elections would depend upon the
vision of the new administration, which may have different priorities. These uncertainties are
exacerbated by the practice of political appointment of key senior financial sector officials
including the head of the Central Bank and federal financial institutions. In view of the
unfinished agenda which lies ahead in terms of financial sector reform, such political uncertainty
could have an impact on the achievement of sustained change, and in the most adverse case,
could allow Brazil to recalibrate Brazil's achievements compared to its vulnerabilities.
176. The drive of the present administration to consolidate and firmly entrench changes prior
to the end of their term, their efforts to build consensus through disclosure and transparency, and
the support and confidence the reform agenda enjoys from the private financial sector
counterbalance these risks. There has been a growing social consensus for the reforms which
are being undertaken, which could help to maintain the present program on course even in
the event of changed political circumstances. For example, the diagnostic undertaken by
independent consultants on the condition of the public banks at the onset of their consolidated
inspection was widely publicized on the Central Bank's website so that the need to address the
issues faced by these institution comes as no surprise to the public. There has also been extensive
public debate on issues such as measures to increase access to financial services, coordinated by
groups such as the Comunidade Soliddria. Payments system reform issues were discussed with
the entire banking system and the present launch date was a consensus decision. Results of the
Central Bank's studies on issues such as interest rate spreads or taxation are all available on its
website. The high degree of transparency of the reform agenda enhances the likelihood of its
sustainability.
Adverse Macroeconomic Circumstances - Domestic and International
177. A deterioration in macroeconomic conditions could complicate economic
management. As in 2001, increased external shocks, including regional contagion due to the
Argentine crisis and weakened investor confidence in the region, could impact adversely on the
exchange rate. Although downward pressure on the exchange rate could help bridge the current
account deficit in the post-1999 floating exchange rate regime, this is less of a concern as foreign
capital inflows continue so far to largely cover the gap. However, FDI flows need to be
sustained. Also, depreciation could tend to fuel inflation thus requiring monetary and/or fiscal
tightening to adhere to inflation targets, as for example, in 2001, through increases in interest
rates or required reserves. The sharp depreciation of the exchange rate and the increase in
inflation above target in 2001 are indicators of remaining vulnerability of the system, as are the
recent revisions upwards (March 2002) of inflation forecasts and targets for 2002 and 2003.
Brazil remains vulnerable to interest-rate and capital-flow shocks due to its debt. Rising spreads
Page 65



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
for emerging market debt and increased external borrowing costs could significantly raise debt
servicing costs.
178.  However, Brazil's foreign currency borrowing spreads opened lower in January 2002
compared to September 2001 (around 820 basis points compared to over 970 in September 2001)
despite a slide from 1500 basis points to over 4000 basis points for Argentina over the same
period. And following the slide of end 2001, end-January 2002 exchange rate also began to edge
higher relative to rates of September 2001. By the beginning of this year, Brazil had restored
some of the ground lost, achieved increased macroeconomic stability and demonstrated its
significant economic robustness against adverse conditions. Two small but significant interest
rate cuts signal the government's confidence, and in the first quarter of 2002, the exchange rate
was steady.
179.  Forecasts in early 2002 are for some strengthening of the real on average against the
dollar in 2002, compared to 2001. Possibilities for further interest rate cuts will depend on price
pressures including the price of oil. It also appears as if the US recession is less significant than
expected in late 2001, and investors appear to have 'decoupled' Brazil from Argentina despite
the deepening Argentine crisis. The government has remained robust against any serious loss of
credibility due to adverse macroeconomic circumstances in 2001. Indeed, the relative strength of
Brazil in the face of the present difficulties faced by Argentina has bolstered confidence in the
policies of the current economic team. So far, if anything crisis conditions have tended to
accelerate the sense of urgency, opening political windows to accelerate reform.
180.  The government has demonstrated its commitment to achieving primary surplus fiscal
targets agreed with the IMF. The primary surplus of R$43.7 billion to end-December 2001
(equivalent to 3.7 percent of GDP), exceeded the target of R$40.2 billion by R$3.5 billion.
Brazil's underlying economic robustness today, compared to the pre-1998 period, may be
attributed to such structural adjustments as the adoption in 1999 of the floating exchange rate
regime, and the Law of Fiscal Responsibility, enacted in mid-2000, which sets tight controls on
expenditure at all levels. In addition to the strong and institutionalized fiscal reforms themselves,
increased credibility has been built with respect to inflation and macroeconomic management,
and improvements have been achieved in the composition of Brazil's public debt through an
active debt management effort.
181. Even in the event of an unforeseen macroeconomic destabilization, the present
operation would continue to have strong justification. The measures supported in the present
operation, which deepen financial markets, rationalize their costs and introduce increased
flexibility and new instruments to enhance the functioning of markets, would serve to aid
stabilization in the face of market turbulence, add to investor confidence, and enhance prospects
for a smooth recovery.
Difficulties in Sustaining Future Stages of Federal Bank Reform
182.  While the first stages of federal bank reform undertaken so far are highly significant, and
there are comprehensive plans for future stages of reform, with improvements in governance,
MIS systems and internal controls, audit, operational efficiency and enhanced profitability, as
well as increased transparency in operations with the government, it may be difficult to
Page 66



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
implement all these stages of reform, which will depend on the adoption of a shared vision by the
banks themselves, the government and the Central Bank. Difficult decisions will arise regarding
business choices, and senior managers both at the federal banks and the Central Bank may
change in the upcoming elections. However, the institutionalization of the principle of enhanced
supervision of these banks, based upon and backed by appropriate prudential regulations, and the
enforcement of these regulations will help protect their future solvency.
183.  The adoption of clear strategic plans by the institutions themselves will also help to
maintain the momentum of reform. The federal banks are already reported to be immersed in
their strategic planning process for the 2002-04 triennial. Internal changes, envisaged to include
improved accountability with decentralized reporting, providing for more objective and
commercial decision making; adoption of a new commercial strategy and new products and
diversification away from traditional targeted sectors and Government-oriented programs; clear
separation of government-related activities; together with improved management information,
internal controls and internal governance, if implemented satisfactorily under the surveillance of
the Central Bank, will clearly reduce risks of backsliding. The clear commitment of the
government, as part of a longer term strategy of diversification away from the federal banking
system as a primary vehicle for the implementation of its social policies, will be key to this
process.
Risk of Institutional Weakness
184.  As noted in the first adjustment loan, some institutional risks remain as several
institutions would be required to contribute to achieve envisaged future reform, both
within and beyond the financial system. Achievement of reforms in some areas such as the
judiciary remains difficult to predict. However, within the financial system, the Central Bank,
principal architect and implementer of the reform program, remains strong and capable.
Moreover, the central regulatory institution in capital markets, Brazil's Securities Commission,
has been given considerably enhanced powers and autonomy with the recent passage of revisions
to the CVM law, and is also now being supported by the Bank's new technical assistance loan
which provides support to mitigate its technical and human resource constraints. In sum, this risk
is perceived to be diminished, and it is not considered likely that this risk will significantly
undermine program implementation.
