Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
provide both technical asistance and credit to new and very small microfinance institutions that
do not qualify for BNDES assistance - thus permitting SEBRAE for the first time to extend
credit. The project plans to reach 30 projects nationwide, initially, both new and existing, across
300 municipalities with low HDI (Human Development Indicators - or IDH, indice de
Desenvolvimento Humano) indices. Loans will be available for up to R$300,000 for 8 years with
a 3 year grace period. Interest rates on SEBRAE lines of credit to MFIs are based on the TJLP
with no spread. According to SEBRAE's data, 13 million Brazilians are excluded from access to
any form of credit, and the new program is destined for this target group.
CHALLENGES FOR THE FUTURE
45.   As the preceding sections show, although Brazil's performance in terms of financial
access at present is fairly average, Brazil is aware of the importance of further increasing access,
in terms of its impact on employment and poverty, and in terms of expanding geographic access.
A number of challenges face Brazil in this context, as demonstrated in the preceding sections.
Key issues which emerge from the preceding discussion are outlined briefly below. More
detailed analysis and evaluation of options will be undertaken in a separate analytic study.'8
Improving the Regional Distribution of Services
46.   As the peceding sections clearly show, the spatial distribution of financial services is
highly unevenly distributed and in general the poorer regions and regions in the North and
Northeast have more limited services. This is even evident in the new technologies, such as
ATMs. However, adjusting for differences in levels of economic activities, the differences are
not as clear. Government efforts to extend services to these areas, for example through the recent
postal service franchise, are commended, but further efforts could be made to identify specific
pockets, in terms of either types of service, or specific municipalities, where service could be
improved.
Increasing Services Offered by Private and Foreign Banks
47.   A second challenge for Brazil will be to increase the role of private and foreign financial
institutions in offering services to small clients and in remote areas. As demonstrated above,
Brazil has largely relied on federal financial institutions so far, for delivering services to more
vulnerable segments - in remote regions, specific subsectors such as agriculture, and to smaller
and thus more likely poorer enterprises or individuals. There are significant differences in the
loan portfolio composition across federal, state, private domestic, and foreign banks. Enticing
private and foreign banks into these areas could need a realignment of incentives and policies
towards both public and private institutions, to ensure improvement of access on a cost-effective
basis.
18 See footnote I above. A study on Access to Financial Services in Brazil being undertaken as Bank AAA, in
collaboration with the Central Bank of Brazil (forthcoming, 2002).
Annex 3 Page 18 of 19



Annex 3: Access to Financial Services
Integrating New Technologies in the Delivery of Financial Services
48.   Developments in information  collection, storage processing  and transmission
technologies (1T technologies) have strongly influenced and continue to influence all aspects of
financial sector activity. Technology potentially influences lower banks' costs by substituting
computers for paper based and labor-intensive methods of accounting for customer deposits,
withdrawals and other transactions and for many internal operations. In addition, they allow
financial institutions to provide services at lower costs through alternative delivery channels for
example through automated teller machines (ATMs), telephone banking and PC banking,
enabling institutions to reach a wider geographic base. Additionally, for small loans, financial
institutions can increase efficiency by devices such as credit scoring models, which use
automated statistical methods to assess default risk of a credit applicant. This reduces costs on
the credit underwriting side since it reduces the role of human evaluation and allows for financial
institutions to underwrite credits of smaller sizes. Authorities could explore impediments to the
development of remote delivery in Brazil which could be due to factors such as the
telecommunications infrastructure or high acquisition costs.
Further Expanding NonBank and Microfinance Services
49.   Finally, as discussed, greater attention can be paid to the expansion of financial
institutions other than banks, including non-banks and microfinance institutions. Brazil's
microfinance institutions operated in a very restrictive policy environment until 1999, and
although several measures have since been initiated to permit the expansion of such institutions,
the limited number of new institutions so far suggest that the impediments to their development
have yet to be fully explored. In this context, many useful proposals have been put up by the
working groups established under the Comunidade Solid4ria, which have been based on
exchanges and discussions with a wide spectrum of civil society. Further proposals suggested
under these working groups would merit attention.

Annex 4: Payments System Reform - Recent Developments
ANNEx 4: PAYMENTS SYSTEM REFORM - RECENT DEVELOPMENTS
THE POSTPONEMENT OF THE LAUNCH OF THE REFORM
1.  In September 2001 the Central Bank of Brazil (Banco Central do Brasil) announced that
the final launch of the new Brazilian large value payments system would be postponed from
October, 2001 to April 22, 2002.
2.   Several reasons were given to justify this decision: (i) tests carried out by the Central Bank
had shown that only three out of the ten largest commercial banks were fully prepared to operate
the new systems (another four were found partially ready, and the last three were even less
prepared); (ii) the several clearinghouses that will integrate the new system were also found
unprepared - only two out of the six active clearinghouses claimed to be ready, another two had
asked for a postponement of one month and the other two had indicated that they would be ready
in March 2002; (iii) the Central Bank was also in a preliminary stage of development of its
applications, due to the delay of hardware for the new payments system, including both the
delivery of the optical fiber system and the installation of the new computer system.
3.   The new timetable is defined in Circular 3060 of the Central Bank, dated September 20,
2001. It has been discussed with and agreed upon by the FEBRABAN (association of banks)
and the Central Bank, and should therefore be realistic. According to the Circular, the new RTGS
(real time gross settlement) system will start operating on February 13, 2002 for operations with
the National Treasury. On April 24, 2002 the RTGS System (Sistema de Transferencia de
Reservas, STR) will be formally launched, even though it will still have transitional features. In
particular, between April 22 and May 17, member banks will be allowed to maintain negative
balances on their accounts during the operating day, provided they do not exceed 100 percent of
their liquid equity (Patrim6nio L(quido Ajustado, PLA), and between May 20 and June 21
overdrafts will not be allowed to exceed 50 percent of the PLA. Finally, on June 24, 2001,
member banks will not be able to run negative balances on their reserve accounts at the Central
Bank and the STR system will assume its final configurations as per its original design.
4.   Circular 3060 also sets.up a timetable for the testing exercise: infrastructure tests will last
until 09-26-2001; system tests until 03-25-2002; capacity tests until 03-27-2002; daily operations
tests until 04-16-2002, and the test of the launch day until 04-17-2002. Finally the Circular
defines the responsibilities and modalities of test monitoring within the Central Bank.'
COMPLETION OF THE REGULATORY / SUPERVISORY FRAMEWORK FOR TBE PAYMENTS SYSTEM
5.   As described in documentation for the first loan,2 the legal framework for the payments
system in Brazil has been established by Law 10214 of March 27, 2001, which converted into
' The Circular also revokes Circular 3032 of May 10, 2001, which contained the previous timetable.
2 See World Bank Report No. P7448-BR; April 26, 2001, on the First Programmatic Financial Sector Adjustmnent
Loan (MOP-PFSECAL-1), Annex 7
Annex 4 Page 1 of 4



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
law several previous Provisional Laws (the first, No. 2008, was issued in December 1999). Law
10214, among other things, (i) defines the payments system and the Central Bank's oversight
responsibility for the payments system over it; (ii) sets up responsibilities and rights for
clearinghouses requiring them to assume in total the counter-party risk vis-a-vis their participants
and the Central Bank, and to protect them against claims on collateral and payment orders
already accepted by the system stemming from bankruptcy procedures; and (iii) provides legal
validation to multilateral netting and excludes explicitly the impact on the payments system of
"zero hour" or similar rules.
6.   Details of the legal framework have been completed by the issue of specific regulations by
the National Monetary Council. In particular, Resolution 2882 of August 30, 2001 defines the
payments system objectives of the Banco Central do Brasil (Article. 1), as efficiency, safety,
integrity, and reliability. It also defines the scope of the application of the Central Bank's rules
and interventions (Article 3), namely all clearinghouses and operators of systems which handle
inter-bank transfers; and settle among at least three direct participants. The core of the
Resolution is the specification of nine general rules which payments system operators must
comply with, that closely resemble the internationally accepted CPSS (Core Principles for
Systemically Important Payments System) (Article 3). Furthermore, according to the Resolution,
the Central Bank will conduct oversight on a continuous basis over the payments system and as
such will (i) regulate operators' activities; (ii) authorize the functioning of the systems; and (iii)
apply sanctions, in the case of non-compliance with the rules. The Resolution also specifies that
specific provisions can be applied by the Central Bank to those systems that are considered
systemically important and clarifies the role of the securities regulator (CVM) and its framework
of cooperation with the Central Bank. Finally, it is indicated that the Central Bank will only
operate payment systems which settle on a gross basis in real time.
7.   Circular 3057 of August 31, 2001, following up on Resolution 2882, approves in detail the
functioning of clearinghouses and other payment system operators and defines several features
which these entities should have in terms of capital requirements, transparency, risk control
measures, operational requirements, etc. All these elements had to be submitted to the Central
Bank by October 1, 2001 for their revision and approval. The Annex to the Circular also defines
a formula to determine whether a payments system is indeed systemically important, based on
the average value of the largest transaction and/or the aggregate value, both over a time span.
8.   The regulatory and supervisory framework for the payments system in Brazil appears at
the moment to be comprehensive and sound. It is worth noting that the department in charge of
the reform within the Central Bank, DEBAN, has expanded its name to the Department of
Banking Operations and Payment Systems, as part of the actions taken to ensure an adequate
organizational framework to manage both the RTGS system and the oversight of clearinghouses
and other system operators.
THE LAUNCH OF THE PRIVATE INTERBANK CLEARINGHOUSE
9.  It appears that a final decision has been made by the banks to launch a private
clearinghouse. The clearinghouse, Camara Interbancdria de Pagamentos, will operate a system
based on net settlement at the end of the day. Further information will need to be acquired on the
timetable and detailed characteristics of this project.

11. To reduce these risks the Central Bank will put in place a mechanism of unremunerated
collateral pre-funding for all checks and DOCs with a value of more than R$5,000 based on a
moving average of the previous two weeks' figures. This should provide a strong disincentive
towards the use of large value items based on debit transfers and, according to the estimates of
the Central Bank, should reduce the amount of large value checks by 80 percent and the amount
of large value DOCs by 97 percent in the first eight months following the RTGS system's
launch. According to the information available, the Circular to regulate these mechanisms is still
under discussion.
TRANSPARENCY OF BANKiNG OPERATIONS3
12. On July 26, 2001, the National Monetary Council enacted Resolution 2878, which
establishes new procedures to be observed by the Brazilian Financial System with regard to the
settlement of financial transactions and services provided to customers and the public in general.
The Resolution aims at improving the relationship between market participants by fostering
additional transparency, discipline, competition and reliability on the part of financial
institutions. In addition, the Resolution consolidates all previous related rules. The main
changes are:
3 Taken from Focus, Banco Central do Brasil, August 2, 2001.
Annex 4 Page 3 of 4



Brazil: Proposed Second Financial Sector Adjustment Loan
* Transparency in the relation between banks and their clients: the new regulation obliges
financial institutions to ensure that clients are fully aware of all contractual clauses,
which, in addition, must also include responsibilities and penalties of both parts, in order
to protect the counterparts against undesirable practices.
* Banks are not allowed to transfer funds of their clients' accounts without previous
consultation.
*  No banking services or operations can be settled if they are tied or conditional to any
other operations or services.
* It is forbidden to release misleading or abusive publicity or information.
* Interest charges must be proportionally reduced in case of anticipated settlement.
* It is forbidden to discriminate against people who are not customers of the bank and to
embarrass customers with debt in arrears.
* Handicapped and senior people have the right to priority attendance.
* Financial institutions cannot deny standard attendance in their branches.
* Customers have the right to withdraw money without postponement if the operation is
carried out in the branch where they maintain their account.
13. International experience shows that such regulations provide strong benefits to the efficient
development of the country's payments system.
OTBER RELATED DEVELOPMENTS
Securities managed by CETIP
14. Circular 3059 of September 20, 2001 provides that all securities managed by CETIP
(Center for the Custody and Financial Liquidation of Private Issues) will have to be settled on the
same day of their maturity or of the maturity of their financial rights (dividends, interests, etc.).
Handling of suspect banknotes
15. A new system for handling suspect banknotes has been in place since June, 2001. The
system allows banks to manage these operations more efficiently with the Central Bank and to be
informed in real time on the status of the investigations. This application will be included in the
STR system, when launched.
Circulars under consultation
16. Some Circulars relating to payments system's issues are under consultation. Among them
a circular to provide access to reserve accounts, at the Central Bank, to investment banks and
similar financial institutions, and a circular to redefine the rediscount procedures.
